Nafaqah — Maintenance
beginner
8 min
Obligation of Wife's Maintenance: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling with proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and legal rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wife's maintenance, identify the condition of entitlement (taslim al-nafs), and derive the ruling from the Quranic verses and hadith cited.

Core Idea
Maintenance is wajib once the wife submits herself – it is the price of her confinement.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling that a wife is entitled to maintenance from her husband. The passage from Kitab al-Nafaqat clearly states the obligation, its condition, and its scope. We will work through the proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and understand the logical basis (ihtibas) that underpins the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm (legal classification) is. The passage rules on nafaqah (maintenance) for the wife: it is wajib.
Wajib means obligatory, but note the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib.
2
Locate the condition
Find the condition that triggers the obligation. The passage states 'idha sallamat nafsaha' – when she submits herself. This is the only condition mentioned.
Taslim al-nafs means moving into the husband's home and making herself available.
3
Examine the Quranic proofs
The author quotes Surah al-Talaq 65:6 and Surah al-Baqarah 2:233. Identify the operative phrase in each verse that indicates the obligation. For example, 'asikinuhunna' implies housing, and 'wa 'ala al-mawludi lahu rizquhunna wa kiswatuhunna' explicitly commands maintenance.
Both verses are used as general proofs.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet's Ḥajjat al-Wadāʿ sermon includes 'wa lahunna 'alaykum rizquhunna wa kiswatuhunna bi al-maʿrūf'. This is a clear command from the Sunnah.
The hadith is reported in Muslim and Abu Dawud.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that submission alone is sufficient. The Ṣāḥibayn require consummation or valid khalwa. Understand the practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, maintenance starts immediately upon the wife moving in; under the Ṣāḥibayn, it starts only after consummation.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah prefers Abu Hanifa's view, and it is the muftā bihī.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

نے فرمایا آدمی عورت سے شادی کرے؟ فرمایا اس کے لئے اس وقت تک نفقہ نہیں ہے (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
Maintenance is obligatory for the wife upon her husband, whether she is Muslim or disbeliever, when she submits herself. ... (detailed explanation with Quranic verses 65:6, 2:233, and hadith from Hajjat al-Wada'). ... Maintenance is the price of confinement. So the wife, having handed herself over, becomes entitled to maintenance, housing, and clothing.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Nafaqat (The Book of Maintenance) establishes the ruling that a wife is entitled to maintenance from her husband. The ruling applies whether the wife is Muslim or non-Muslim (e.g., Kitabiyya). The condition for this obligation is that the wife submits herself (taslim al-nafs) to her husband, i.e., moves into his house and makes herself available to him. Maintenance includes food, clothing, and housing. The author defines nafaqah linguistically as 'giving food etc.', and then lists those who are entitled: wife, divorced woman, children, parents, and relatives. The proofs are from the Quran (Surah al-Talaq 65:6 and Surah al-Baqarah 2:233) and from the Prophet's Hajjat al-Wada' sermon. The underlying rationale is that maintenance is a compensation for the wife's confinement (ihtibas) to her husband's home; therefore, she must first submit herself. An athar from 'Ata' is cited: 'no maintenance for a woman until her husband consummates the marriage' (i.e., only after full submission).

Key Terms
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance including food, clothing, and housing for the wife (and other dependents).
احتباس (ihtibas): The wife's confinement to her husband's home for marital relations.
تسليم النفس (taslim al-nafs): The wife's submission to the husband (handing herself over) by residing in his home and not withholding herself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the condition for a wife to be entitled to maintenance from her husband?
A) The couple must have consummated the marriage
B) The wife must submit herself to her husband by moving into his house
C) The wife must be Muslim
D) The husband must have agreed to pay maintenance in the marriage contract

Key Takeaway
Maintenance for the wife is wajib upon the husband from the moment she submits herself to his house, based on Quran, Sunnah, and the rationale of ihtibas.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
beginner
6 min
When Does Wife's Maintenance Become Wajib?
Ruling with proof on obligation of wife's maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a wife becomes entitled to nafaqah and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish its obligation.

Core Idea
Wife's nafaqah is wajib upon surrender to the husband.

In this lesson we examine the ruling that the wife's maintenance (nafaqah) becomes obligatory upon the husband when she surrenders herself to his custody. The author of Al-Sharh al-Thamiri presents the ruling, then supports it with Quranic verses and Prophetic hadith, and explains the rationale that nafaqah is badal al-ihtibas (compensation for confinement). We will walk through the ruling, its conditions, and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the wife's nafaqah (maintenance). The ruling is wajib upon the husband when the wife surrenders herself (taslim al-nafs) to his home.
Nafaqah includes food, clothing, and housing according to custom.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 65:6-7 (lodging and spending on wives and pregnant women), Quran 2:233 (provision and clothing for nursing mothers), and the Prophet's hadith in the Farewell Pilgrimage: 'They have upon you their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable.'
Also an athar from 'Ata' clarifying that nafaqah is not due before consummation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'anfiqoo' in the Quran indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul. The hadith explicitly commands provision and clothing.
The evidence is considered zanni al-dalala, hence the ruling is wajib, not fard.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require consummation or valid retirement for nafaqah to become obligatory. The Hanafi school holds that surrender alone suffices.
The athar of 'Ata' is interpreted differently; Hanafi scholars see it as supporting the trigger of surrender.
5
Understand the rationale: badal al-ihtibas
Nafaqah is compensation for the wife's confinement (ihtibas) in the husband's home. Once she surrenders, the husband is obligated to provide maintenance in exchange for her availability.
This explains why nafaqah is not due when the wife is nashiz (disobedient) or before surrender.

Source Text

نفقہ احتباس کا بدلہ ہے۔ اس لئے عورت نے اپنے آپ کو سپرد کر دیا تو شوہر پر اس کا بدلہ نفقہ سکنی اور کپڑ الا زم ہو گیا جو اس معاشرے میں چلتا ہے (۲) اوپر آیت گزری۔ على المولود له رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف (آیت ۲۳۳ سورۃ البقر (۲) اور حدیث بھی گزری۔ ولهن عليكم رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف (ج) (مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۳۹۴ نمبر ۱۳۱۸) جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیوی کا نفقہ شوہر پر لازم ہے۔ اپنے آپ کو سپرد کرنے پر نفقہ لازم ہو گا اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن عطاء في الرجل يتزوج المرأة قال لا نفقة لها حتى يدخل بها (د) (مصنف ابن الى هيئة 199 مقالوافي الرجل يتزوج المرأة فتطلب النفقة قبل ان يدخل بها هل لها ذلك حاشیہ : (الف) جہاں تم رہو اپنی گنجائز کے مطابق وہیں بیوی کو رکھو۔ اور ان کو تکلیف نہ دو تنگ کرنے کے لئے۔ اور اگر حاملہ ہیں تو ان پر خرچ کرد وضع حمل تک ، پس اگر تمہارے لئے دودھ پلائے تو ان کو ان کی اجرت دو اور معروف کے ساتھ ان سے مشورہ کرو (ب) عورتوں کا تم پر نفقہ اور کپڑا ہے مناسب انداز میں (ج) عورتوں کا تم پر نفقہ اور کپڑا ہے مناسب انداز میں (1) حضرت عطاء نے فرمایا آدمی عورت سے شادی کرے؟ فرمایا اس کے لئے اس وقت تک نفقہ نہیں ہے (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )

Book of Nafaqat. [2128] (1) Maintenance is obligatory for the wife upon her husband, whether she is Muslim or disbeliever, when she surrenders herself. Book of Nafaqat. Essential note: Giving food etc. to someone is called nafaqah. Nafaqah is for the wife, for the divorced woman, for children, for parents, and for dhawi al-arham. Its proof is in this verse: 'Lodge them where you lodge according to your means, and do not harm them to straiten them. And if they are pregnant, then spend on them until they give birth. Then if they nurse for you, give them their wages, and consult among yourselves in kindness. And if you disagree, then another will nurse for him. Let a man of wealth spend according to his wealth, and he whose provision is restricted, let him spend from what Allah has given him. Allah does not burden a soul except [according to] what He has given it. Allah will bring about, after hardship, ease.' (Surah at-Talaq 65) This verse mentions in detail the lodging and maintenance of a pregnant woman. (2) In another verse: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:233) This verse mentions the food, maintenance and clothing of the nursing woman. (3) The Prophet (peace be upon him) gave a long speech during the Farewell Pilgrimage, part of which is: 'And they have upon you their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable.' (Muslim, Sharif, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 394 no. 1218; Abu Dawud, Sharif, Bab Safhat Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 269 no. 1905) From this hadith it is also known that for the wife, appropriate daily provision and clothing are obligatory upon the husband. [2128] (1) Maintenance is obligatory for the wife upon her husband, whether she is Muslim or disbeliever, when she surrenders herself to his house. Then upon him is her maintenance, her clothing, and her housing. Whether the wife is Muslim or ahl al-kitab, when she has handed herself over to the husband, the husband is obligated to provide her maintenance, clothing, and housing. Maintenance is the compensation for confinement. Therefore, when the woman has surrendered herself, the husband becomes obligated to give her compensation: maintenance, housing, and clothing according to the custom of that society. (2) The verse passed above: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:233) And the hadith also passed: 'And they have upon you their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable.' (Muslim, Sharif, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p. 394 no. 1318) From this it is known that the wife's maintenance is obligatory upon the husband. The evidence that maintenance becomes obligatory upon surrender is this athar: 'From Ata, regarding a man who marries a woman, he said: She has no maintenance until he has intercourse with her.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 199, Mawaqif al-Rajul al-Mutazawwij al-Mar'ah fa Talab al-Nafaqah qabl an Yadkhula biha hal laha dhalik) Footnote: (a) Lodge them where you lodge according to your means... (b) Women have upon you provision and clothing in a suitable manner. (c) Women have upon you provision and clothing in a suitable manner. (1) Hadrat Ata said: A man marries a woman? He said: She has no maintenance until he has intercourse with her. (Remaining on next page) [PAGE_210] Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Vol. 3, p. 205, Book of Nafaqat. 'In his house, then upon him is her maintenance, her clothing, and her housing.' [2129] (2) That is considered by the condition of both of them, whether the husband is wealthy or poor. 130 (3) If she refrains from surrendering herself until he gives her... J. Rabi' p. 175, no. 19018) From this athar it is known that before surrender, the wife is not entitled to maintenance.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the obligation of the wife's maintenance. The author begins by stating the ruling: maintenance (nafaqah) is wajib upon the husband for his wife when she surrenders herself to him (taslim al-nafs). This applies whether the wife is Muslim or non-Muslim. The author then provides proofs from the Quran: Surat al-Talaq (65:6-7) regarding lodging and maintenance of pregnant women, and Surat al-Baqarah (2:233) regarding provision and clothing for nursing women. A hadith from the Farewell Pilgrimage is also cited: the Prophet said, 'They have upon you their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable.' The author explains that nafaqah is compensation (badal) for the wife's confinement (ihtibas) in the husband's home. Therefore, upon her surrender, the husband must provide maintenance, clothing, and housing according to local custom. The author also cites an athar from 'Ata' which clarifies that nafaqah is not due before consummation, implying that surrender before consummation does not trigger the obligation—rather actual entry is required. This distinguishes the starting point of the obligation.

Key Terms
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance: food, clothing, housing, and other necessities provided to the wife (or others) by the husband.
تسلیم نفس (taslim al-nafs): The wife's act of surrendering herself to the husband's custody, making herself available for marriage rights.
احتباس (ihtibas): Confinement or retention of the wife in the husband's home; the basis for nafaqah being compensation for her being at his disposal.
بدل الاحتباس (badal al-ihtibas): Compensation for confinement; the legal basis for nafaqah in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a wife become entitled to nafaqah from her husband?
A) Immediately after the marriage contract is concluded.
B) When she surrenders herself to her husband at his home.
C) Only after consummation of the marriage.
D) Only if she is Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Wife's nafaqah is wajib upon surrender to the husband, supported by Quran and Sunnah.

Nafaqah — Maintenance

Measure of Maintenance: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explains that nafaqah amount depends on both spouses' status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on how nafaqah (maintenance) is quantified and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using dalil.

Core Idea
Nafaqah is determined by both spouses' status, not just the husband's wealth — a moderate amount is wajib.

This passage presents a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the measure of maintenance (nafaqah). The Hanafis hold that the amount must be moderate, considering the condition of both husband and wife, while the Shafi'is focus solely on the husband's means. The author supports the Hanafi view with a hadith of Hind bint Utbah, then presents the Shafi'i evidence from Quran and hadith. Understanding this dispute helps us appreciate how different usul principles lead to different fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi ruling is that the amount of nafaqah is determined by the condition of both spouses, leading to a moderate amount (al-wasat).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only the husband's condition matters: if he is wealthy, he gives the maintenance of the wealthy; if poor, the maintenance of the poor.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i evidence includes Quran 65:7 (spend according to capacity) and the hadith 'Feed them from what you eat' – both focus on the husband's ability.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond implicitly: the Shafi'i proofs are general and do not exclude considering the wife's status. The specific hadith of Hind shows that when the wife's status is higher, the standard is ma'ruf, which includes her needs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, if a wealthy husband marries a poor woman, the Hanafis give a moderate amount (less than wealthy, more than poor), while the Shafi'is give the full wealthy amount regardless of her status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۱۲۹] (٢) يعتبر ذلك بحالهما جميعا موسرا كان الزوج او معسرا ۱۳۰ (۳) فان امتنعت من تسليم نفسها حتى يعطيها
(۲۱۲۹) (۲) نفقے کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا دونوں کی حالتوں سے مالدار ہو شوہر یا تنگدست ۔ حنفیہ کے نزدیک یہ نہیں ہے کہ شوہر مالدار ہے تو اس کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے مالدار کا نفقہ لازم ہو بلکہ دونوں کے درمیان کا نفقہ لازم ہوگا۔ مثلا شو ہر مالدار ہے اور عورت غریب ہو تو مالدار سے کم اور غریب سے زیادہ کا نفقہ لازم ہوگا۔
حدیث میں ہے۔ قالت هند يا رسول الله ان ابا سفيان رجل شحيح فهل على جناح ان آخذ من ماله ما يكفيني وبني ؟ قال خذى بالمعروف (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب وعلی الوارث مثل ذلک ص ۸۰۸ نمبر ۵۳۷۰) اس حدیث میں عورت کی حیثیت زیادہ تھی اور شوہر کم دے رہے تھے تو آپ نے معروف کے ساتھ زیادہ نفقہ لینے کی اجازت دی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ درمیانہ نفقہ لازم ہوگا۔
نانه امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ نفقہ میں مرد کی حالت کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ یعنی مرد مالدار ہے تو مالدار کا نفقہ لازم ہوگا اور غریب ہے تو غریب کا نفقہ لازم ہوگا۔
آیت میں ہے۔ لینفق ذو سعة من سعته ومن قدر عليه رزقه فلينفق مما آتاه الله لا يكلف الله ندسا الا ما آتاها (ب) ( آیت سے سورۃ اطلاق (۶۵) اس آیت میں شوہر کو مخاطب کر کے کہا کہ اپنی وسعت کے مطابق خرچ کرے۔ اور یہ بھی کہا کہ جس پر تنگی ہو گئی ہو وہ اللہ کیمال میں سے خرچ کرے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ شوہر کی حالت کے اعتبار سے نفقہ لازم ہوگا۔ عن جده معاوية القشیری قال اتيت رسول الله قال فقلت ما تقول فى نسائنا قال اطعموهن مما تأكلون واكسوهن مما تكتسون (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی حق المرأة على زوجها ص ۲۹۸ نمبر ۲۱۴۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جو کھاتے ہو وہ کھلا ؤ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرد کا عتبار ہے۔
[2129] (2) That is considered by the condition of both of them, whether the husband is wealthy or poor. (2) The measure of maintenance will be considered from both conditions, whether the husband is wealthy or poor. According to the Hanafis, it is not that if the husband is wealthy, then the maintenance of the wealthy is obligatory, but rather the maintenance between the two will be obligatory. For example, if the husband is wealthy and the woman is poor, then a maintenance less than that of a wealthy and more than that of a poor will be obligatory. In a hadith: 'Hind said, O Messenger of Allah, Abu Sufyan is a stingy man; is there any sin on me if I take from his wealth enough for me and my children? He said: Take according to what is acceptable.' (Bukhari, Sharif, Bab wa 'Ala al-Warith Mithl Dhalik, p. 808 no. 5370) In this hadith, the woman's status was higher and the husband was giving less; so the Prophet permitted taking more maintenance according to what is acceptable. From this it is known that moderate maintenance is obligatory. Then Imam Shafi'i says that in maintenance, the condition of the man will be considered; that is, if the man is wealthy, the maintenance of the wealthy is obligatory, and if poor, the maintenance of the poor is obligatory. In the verse: 'Let a man of wealth spend according to his wealth, and he whose provision is restricted, let him spend from what Allah has given him. Allah does not burden a soul except [according to] what He has given it.' (Surah at-Talaq 65:7) In this verse, the husband is addressed, saying he should spend according to his capacity, and also said that the one in straitened circumstances should spend from what Allah has given him. This means that maintenance is obligatory according to the husband's condition. From Muawiyah al-Qushayri: 'I came to the Messenger of Allah and said, 'What do you say about our women?' He said: 'Feed them from what you eat and clothe them from what you wear.' (Abu Dawud, Sharif, Bab Haqq al-Mar'ah 'ala Zawjiha, p. 298 no. 2144) In this hadith it says: Feed them what you eat; from this it is known that the man's condition is considered.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage contains an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the measure of maintenance (nafaqah). The ruling states that the amount of maintenance is to be determined by considering the condition of both the husband and wife. The author explains that according to the Hanafis, it is not simply that a wealthy husband must give the maintenance of the wealthy, but rather a moderate amount between the two extremes: if the husband is wealthy and the wife is poor, the maintenance should be less than what a wealthy person would give to a wealthy wife, and more than what a poor person would give. The proof is from the hadith of Hind bint Utbah: when she complained that Abu Sufyan was miserly, the Prophet permitted her to take 'according to what is acceptable' (al-ma'ruf), which implies a moderate amount considering her needs. The author then presents the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that only the husband's condition is considered: if he is wealthy, he gives the maintenance of the wealthy; if poor, the maintenance of the poor. The Shafi'i evidence includes the Quranic verse (65:7) which commands spending according to capacity, and the hadith 'Feed them from what you eat and clothe them from what you wear,' which links the wife's maintenance to the husband's own consumption. The Hanafi response is implicit: the verse and hadith are not exclusive; the hadith of Hind shows consideration of the wife's needs as well. The Hanafi school uses istihsan and the principle of moderation (al-wasat) to require a standard that is fair to both parties.

Key Terms
معروف (ma'ruf): What is recognized as reasonable and customary in the society; the standard for maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only by the husband's wealth or poverty.
B) Only by the wife's social status.
C) By the condition of both husband and wife, resulting in a moderate amount.
D) By the minimum wage set by the government.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines nafaqah by considering both spouses' status, requiring a moderate amount that is fair to both, in contrast to the Shafi'i focus solely on the husband.

Wife's Nafaqah When Withholding Surrender for Mahr
Ruling on nafaqah when wife withholds for mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wife's nafaqah when she refuses surrender until mahr is paid and explain the legal reasoning (that it is not nushuz).

Core Idea
Refusing surrender for mahr is not nushuz; constructive surrender preserves nafaqah.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where a wife withholds herself from her husband's custody until he pays her the mahr. The key question is whether she still deserves maintenance (nafaqah). The Hanafi school rules that she does, because her refusal is for a legitimate right, not disobedience. This protects the wife from losing maintenance while asserting her right to the dower.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the case: wife refuses to surrender herself until husband pays mahr. Recognize that mahr is the wife's exclusive right due upon marriage.
2
Identify the legal issue
The issue is whether this refusal constitutes nushuz (disobedience) that would nullify her right to nafaqah.
Nushuz is key: it negates nafaqah.
3
Analyze the ruling
The text rules nafaqah remains wajib. Reason: refusal is for mahr, which is her right, not mere disobedience. She is considered constructively surrendered.
Constructive surrender: because the only barrier is the husband's default.
4
Examine cross-madhhab perspective
Note that some other schools might require physical surrender or a qadhi order for nafaqah to continue. The Hanafi view is more protective of the wife's rights.
5
Apply to related scenarios
Consider if the wife refuses for another legitimate right (e.g., her share of inheritance) – similar principle likely applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) فان امتنعت من تسليم نفسها حتى يعطيها
[۲۱۳۰] (۳) اگر عورت باز رہے اپنے آپ کو سپرد کرنے سے یہاں تک کہ اس کو مہر دے تو اس کے لئے نفقہ ہے۔ عورت اپنے آپ کو اس لئے سپرد نہیں کر رہی ہے کہ مہر دے تب اپنے آپ کو سپرد کروں گی تو اس صورت میں عورت کو نفقہ ملے گا۔ اس لئے کہ عورت اپنے حق کی وجہ سے سپردنہیں کر رہی ہے اس لئے وہ ناشزہ نہیں ہوئی اور گویا کہ سپرد کر دیا اس لئے اس کو نفقہ ملے گا۔
(3) If she refrains from surrendering herself until he gives her... [2130] (3) If the woman refrains from surrendering herself until he gives her the mahr, then she has maintenance. The woman is not surrendering herself because she says 'Give me the mahr, then I will surrender'. In this case, the woman will receive maintenance because she is not surrendering due to her own right (mahr); therefore she is not nashiz (disobedient), and it is as if she has surrendered. So maintenance is due to her.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This is a ruling on a specific scenario: the wife withholds herself from the husband's custody until he pays her the mahr (dower). The ruling states that in such a case, she is still entitled to maintenance (nafaqah). The author explains the reasoning: the wife is not refusing out of disobedience (nushuz), but because she is asserting her right to the mahr, which is her exclusive property. Since the mahr is a separate obligation owed by the husband, her refusal to surrender until it is paid does not negate her right to maintenance. In Hanafi fiqh, the wife's surrender (taslim) is the basis for nafaqah, but here she is considered to have constructively surrendered because the only reason she has not physically surrendered is the husband's default in paying the mahr. Therefore, she is not nashiz, and maintenance continues to be wajib. This ruling protects the wife from being caught in a catch-22 where she would lose maintenance if she insists on her mahr before surrender.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushuz): Disobedience of the wife to her husband's lawful rights, which nullifies her right to nafaqah.
مهر (mahr): The dower paid by the husband to the wife, her exclusive property.
تمكين (tamkin): The wife's submission and availability for the marital relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only entitled to nafaqah if she has a court order.
D) Not nashiz but still loses nafaqah until she physically surrenders.

Key Takeaway
A wife's refusal to surrender for her right of mahr does not nullify her right to nafaqah in the Hanafi school.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Maintenance for a Disobedient Wife (Nushuz)
States the ruling and provides hadith/athar evidence for nushuz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a wife loses her right to maintenance and explain the legal basis using the Hanafi principle of ihtibas.

Core Idea
A wife's maintenance depends on her ihtibas; if she abandons it through disobedience, she forfeits support.

In this passage, we learn a crucial rule of family law: the wife's right to maintenance is not unconditional. It is tied to her role in the marital home. When she leaves in disobedience (nushuz), the basis for maintenance—her confinement (ihtibas)—is broken. The text provides strong evidence from the hadith of Fatimah bint Qais and the practice of the Companions, showing that this principle is rooted in the Sunnah. By the end, you will be able to apply this rule to real situations and understand its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Read the opening sentence: 'وان نشزت فلا نفقة لها حتى تعود الى منزله'. Note that the ruling is negative (no maintenance) and conditional upon nushuz. The condition for restoration is return to the house.
The term 'نشزت' refers to specific legal disobedience, not mere disagreement.
2
Understand the rationale: ihtibas
The Urdu commentary states that maintenance is due because of ihtibas (confinement). When the wife leaves in disobedience, ihtibas ends, so maintenance ceases. Grasp this causal link: nafaqah is in exchange for ihtibas.
Hanafi fiqh treats nafaqah as a reciprocal obligation, not a pure charity.
3
Analyze the first evidence: Hadith of Fatimah bint Qais
Read the hadith (Abu Dawud). Fatimah was divorced irrevocably and left the house. The Prophet said she had no maintenance. This is the primary proof: separation from marital authority voids the right to support.
The case involves divorce, but Hanafi jurists analogize nushuz to this because the effect (loss of ihtibas) is the same.
4
Analyze the second evidence: Athar of al-Sha'bi
Read the athar: a woman who leaves disobediently has no maintenance even if she stays away for twenty years. This reinforces that duration does not matter; the cause is disobedience.
This shows the strength of the Hanafi position: the right is lost immediately upon nushuz.
5
Apply the ruling: restoration upon return
The text explicitly says 'حتى تعود' (until she returns). Maintenance is restored when she comes back, regardless of whether she has repented. The condition is objective: physical return.
This distinguishes Hanafi ruling from views that require evidence of obedience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان نشزت فلا نفقة لها حتى تعود الى منزله

۲۱۳۱] (۴) اور اگر نافرمانی کی تو اس کے لئے نفقہ نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ گھر نہ لوٹ آئے۔ عورت نے نافرمانی کی اور گھر سے نکل گئی تو اب اس کے لئے نفقہ نہیں ہے جب تک کہ گھر واپس نہ آئے۔ نا فرمان عورت کا احتباس نہیں رہا اور نفقہ احتباس کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے لئے نفقہ نہیں ہو گا (۲) ایک عورت نے نافرمانی کی تو اس کو نفقہ نہیں ملا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن فاطمة بنت قيس ان ابا عمرو بن الحفص طلقها البتة وهو غائب فارسل اليها وکیله بشعير فتسخطته فقال والله مالك علينا من شيء فجائترسول الله فذكرت ذلك له فقال لها ليس لك عليه نفقة (الف) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی نفقة المتبوت ص ۳۱۸ نمبر ۲۲۸۴) دوسرے اثر میں ہے۔ عـن ســلـيـمـان ابن یسار في خروج فاطمة قال انما كان ذلك من سوء الخلق (ب) ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من انکر ذلک علی فاطمہ بنت قیس ص ۳۲۰ نمبر ۲۲۹۴ ر مسلم شریف ، باب المطلقة البائن لا نفقة لصاص ۴۸۳ نمبر ۱۳۸۰) اس حدیث میں عورت نے شوہر کے وکیل کے ساتھ بد زبانی کی تو اس کو نفقہ نہیں دیا گیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ نا فرمان عورت کے لئے نفقہ نہیں ہے، ہاں ! گھر واپس آ جائے تو اس کو نفقہ ملے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن الشعبى انه سئل عن امرأة خرجت من بيتها عاصية لزوجها الها نفقة ؟ قال لا وان مكثت عشرين سنة (ج) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۲۰۰ ما قالوافي المرأة تخرج من بیتھا وھی عاصیة لزوجها الها النفقة ج رابع ، ص ۱۷۶، نمبر ۱۹۰۲۳/ مصنف عبدالرزاق نمبر ۱۲۳۵۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نافرمانی کر کے نکل جائے تو اس کے لئے نفقہ نہیں ہے۔

نشرت : نافرمانی کرنا، تعود : واپس لوٹنا۔

حاشیہ : (الف) عمرو بن حفص نے بائنہ طلاق دی اس حال میں کہ وہ غائب تھے، پس اس کے وکیل نے جو بھیجا تو فاطمہ بنت قیس غصہ ہوگئی تو عمر نے فرمایا خدا کی قسم تمہارا مجھ پر کوئی حق نہیں ہے، پھر وہ حضور کے پاس آئی اور اس کا تذکرہ کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا تمہارا اس پر نفقہ نہیں ہے (ب) سلیمان بن یسار فاطمہ کے نکلنے کے بارے میں فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ اس کی بداخلاقی کی وجہ سے ہوا ( ج ) حضرت شعمی سے عورت کے بارے میں پوچھا جو شوہر کی نافرمان ہو کر گھر سے نکل گئی ہو کیا اس کو نفقہ ملے گا ؟ فرمایا نہیں! اگر چہ میں سال تک وہ ٹھہری رہے
And if she commits nushuz, then there is no maintenance for her until she returns to his house. [Urdu:] And if she commits disobedience, then there is no maintenance for her until she returns home. A woman committed disobedience and left the house, so now there is no maintenance for her until she returns home. The disobedient woman's confinement (ihtibas) is no longer present, and maintenance is due because of confinement. Therefore, she has no maintenance. (2) A woman committed disobedience, so she was not given maintenance. In the hadith: from Fatimah bint Qais that Abu Amr ibn Hafs divorced her irrevocably while he was absent, so he sent his agent to her with barley, and she was angry with him, so he said, 'By Allah, you have no right from us.' Then she came to the Messenger of Allah and mentioned that to him, and he said to her, 'You have no maintenance from him.' (a) (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Maintenance of the Divorced Woman, p. 318, no. 2284). Another athar: from Sulayman ibn Yasar regarding Fatimah's leaving, he said, 'That was only due to bad character.' (b) (Abu Dawud, Chapter on those who rejected that concerning Fatimah bint Qais, p. 320, no. 2294, and Muslim, Chapter on the Irrevocably Divorced Woman has no Maintenance, p. 483, no. 1380). In this hadith, the woman used bad language with the husband's agent, so she was not given maintenance, which indicates that the disobedient wife has no maintenance. Yes, if she returns home, she will receive maintenance. (2) In another athar: from al-Sha'bi that he was asked about a woman who left her house disobedient to her husband, does she have maintenance? He said, 'No, even if she stays for twenty years.' (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 200, Section on what they said about a woman who leaves her house while disobedient to her husband, does she have maintenance? Vol. 4, p. 176, no. 19023; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 12352). This athar indicates that if she leaves in disobedience, she has no maintenance. Nushuz: disobedience; ta'ud: returns. Footnotes: (a) Abu Amr ibn Hafs gave an irrevocable divorce while he was absent, then his agent sent something to Fatimah bint Qais, and she became angry, so Umar said, 'By Allah, you have no right on us.' Then she came to the Prophet and mentioned that, so he said, 'You have no maintenance from him.' (b) Sulayman ibn Yasar said regarding Fatimah's leaving, 'That was only due to her bad character.' (c) Al-Sha'bi was asked about a woman who left her house disobedient to her husband, does she have maintenance? He said, 'No, even if she stays for twenty years.'

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on nafaqah for a wife who is nashiz (disobedient). The ruling is clear: a disobedient wife loses her right to maintenance until she returns to her husband's home. The rationale is that maintenance is due in exchange for the wife's ihtibas (placing herself under her husband's authority/availability). When she leaves in disobedience, the ihtibas is broken. The passage provides strong evidence from the hadith of Fatimah bint Qais and the athar of al-Sha'bi, both confirming that a wife who leaves in disobedience has no claim to maintenance. The text also distinguishes between simple leaving and returning; once she returns, maintenance is restored. The footnotes clarify the key terms: nushuz means disobedience, and ta'ud means to return. The hadith of Fatimah is particularly instructive: she left the house after an irrevocable divorce and was told she had no maintenance. The Hanafi scholars apply this principle analogically to a wife who leaves in disobedience during an ongoing marriage.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushūz): Disobedience of the wife towards her husband, specifically leaving the marital home without a valid reason.
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter, that a husband is obliged to provide for his wife.
احتباس (ihtibās): The wife's confinement to the husband's home and her availability for his legitimate purposes, which is the basis for her right to maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a wife regain her right to maintenance after committing nushuz?
A) When she apologizes to her husband.
B) When she returns to the marital home.
C) When she is no longer angry.
D) When she begins to obey again.

Key Takeaway
A wife's right to maintenance is conditional upon her ihtibas; if she commits nushuz, she loses that right until she returns.

Maintenance for a Young Wife: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Presents the Hanafi ruling and the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a young wife's maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a young wife too young for intercourse receives no maintenance, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Maintenance is tied to the possibility of enjoyment, not mere surrender.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on maintenance of a minor wife. The Hanafi school conditions maintenance on the wife's capacity for sexual enjoyment, while the Shafi'i school bases it on the apparent act of surrender. Understanding this difference illuminates how each school prioritizes effective cause versus textual generality.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: a young wife who cannot be enjoyed has no maintenance even if she surrenders. Understand the effective cause (illa): the possibility of istimta'.
The Hanafi school views ihtibas (confinement) as ineffective if enjoyment is impossible.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that maintenance is due because she has surrendered, establishing apparent ihtibas.
Shafi'i relies on the generality of the Quranic command for maintenance.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is the general hadith: 'ولهن عليكم رزقهن' (maintenance is obligatory for all wives).
They also argue that surrender creates a binding obligation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school restricts the general text using the athar of 'Ata: 'لا نفقة لها حتى يدخل بها' (no maintenance until consummation). This shows the illa is capability of enjoyment.
Hanafi uses takhsis (restriction) of the general by a more specific evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: In Hanafi, a 6-year-old wife gets no maintenance until puberty; in Shafi'i, she gets maintenance from the moment of surrender.
The dispute has significant financial implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانت صغيرة لا يُستمتع بها فلا نفقة لها وان سلمت اليه نفسها

مثلا چھ سات سال کی بچی ہو جس سے صحبت کرنا ناممکن ہو۔ اگر اس نے اپنے آپ کو شوہر کے حوالے کردیا پھر بھی س کو نفقہ نہیں ملے گا۔ حوالے کرنے کا مقصد یہ تھا کہ اس سے فائدہ اٹھایا جا سکتا ہو۔ اور جب اس سے فائدہ نہیں اٹھایا جا سکتا ہو تو گویا کہ احتباس نہیں ہوا اس لئے اس کے لئے نفقہ نہیں ہوگا۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن عطاء فی الرجل يتزوج المرأة قال لا نفقة لها حتى يدخل بها ( و ) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۱۹۹ ما قالوافي الرجل يتزوج المرأة فتطلب النفقة قبل ان يدخل بها هل لها ذلك؟ ج رابع ، ص ۱۷۵، نمبر ۱۹۰۱۸ کتاب الآثار لامام محمد ، باب نفقه التي لم يدخل بها ص ۱۲ نمبر ۵۱۹)

امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ چونکہ عورت شوہر کے گھر جا چکی ہے اور حوالے کر چکی ہے اس لئے ظاہری طور پر احتباس ہو گیا اس لئے چاہے اس سے فائدہ نہ اٹھا سکتا ہو پھر بھی اس کے لئے نفقہ ہوگا۔ حديث ولهن عليكم رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف (مسلم شریف نمبر ۱۲۱۸) میں بالغ اور نابالغ بیوی کا فرق نہیں کیا بلکہ ہر قسم کی بیوی کے لئے نفقہ لازم کیا اس لئے صغیرہ کے لئے بھی نفقہ ہوگا۔

حاشیہ : (د) حضرت عطاء نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی شادی کرے تو اس وقت اس کے لئے نفقہ نہیں ہے جب تک صحبت نہ کر لے۔
And if she is young and cannot be enjoyed, then there is no maintenance for her even if she surrenders herself to him. [Urdu:] For example, a girl of six or seven years with whom intercourse is impossible. If she surrenders herself to her husband, even then she will not receive maintenance. The purpose of surrender was that she could be benefited from, and when benefit is not possible, it is as if ihtibas has not occurred, so she has no maintenance. In one athar: from 'Ata regarding a man who marries a woman, he said, 'She has no maintenance until he has intercourse with her.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 199, Section on what they said about a man who marries a woman and she seeks maintenance before he has intercourse with her, does she have that? Vol. 4, p. 175, no. 19018; Kitab al-Athar of Imam Muhammad, Chapter on Maintenance of the Woman with whom he has not Consummated, p. 112, no. 519). Imam al-Shafi'i said that since the woman has gone to the husband's house and has surrendered, apparent ihtibas has occurred, so even if he cannot benefit from her, she still has maintenance. The hadith 'You are obliged to provide for them and clothe them in a reasonable manner' (Muslim, no. 1218) does not differentiate between an adult and a minor wife; rather, it makes maintenance obligatory for every type of wife, so a minor wife also has maintenance. Footnote: (d) 'Ata said: If a man marries a woman, she has no maintenance until he has intercourse with her.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a wife who is so young that she cannot be sexually enjoyed. The Hanafi ruling is that she is not entitled to maintenance even if she has placed herself under the husband's authority, because the effective cause (illa) for maintenance is the possibility of enjoyment (istimta'). Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since she has surrendered, ihtibas is established and maintenance becomes due. The Hanafi response is that the general Quranic command for maintenance is qualified by custom and the reality of the marriage; the hadith 'ولهن عليكم رزقهن' applies to wives who can be enjoyed. The athar from 'Ata reinforces that maintenance does not become obligatory until after consummation. This is a classic example of the Hanafi emphasis on the effective cause and the Shafi'i emphasis on the general text. The footnote further supports the Hanafi position by quoting 'Ata that maintenance is tied to consummation.

Key Terms
صغيرة (ṣaghīrah): A minor wife who has not reached the age where intercourse is physically possible, typically under nine years of age.
استمتاع (istimtā‘): Sexual enjoyment/benefit that a husband can derive from his wife, which is the basis for the obligation of maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on maintenance for a wife who is too young for intercourse but has surrendered to her husband?
A) She gets maintenance because she surrendered.
B) She gets no maintenance until she becomes capable of intercourse.
C) She gets maintenance only if the husband is also a minor.
D) She gets maintenance if she demands it.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, maintenance for a wife is conditional on the possibility of sexual enjoyment, not mere surrender or residence.

Ruling on Maintenance When the Husband Is Too Young
States the ruling and provides evidence for maintenance when the husband is a minor but the wife is adult

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance when the husband is a minor unable to consummate, and explain the legal basis using the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Core Idea
An adult wife receives maintenance from her minor husband because she has surrendered (ihtibas) — the delay is his, not hers.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: what happens when the husband is too young to consummate the marriage, but the wife is adult and has surrendered herself. The Hanafi school rules that maintenance is obligatory on the husband, based on the principle that the wife's duty is to surrender, not to ensure consummation. We will examine the source text and the evidence from the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The subject is a husband who is a minor ('saghir') and cannot have intercourse, and a wife who is adult ('kabirah'). The ruling is explicit: she has maintenance from his wealth.
2
Understand the legal reason
The Urdu commentary explains that the wife has surrendered herself (ihtibas). Because she performed her duty, maintenance is due even though the husband cannot benefit.
ihtibas = surrendering oneself for marital relations.
3
Examine the dalil
The athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i states: if the delay is from the man, he pays maintenance; if from the woman, she gets none. Here the delay is from the husband, so maintenance is due.
The athar is from Kitab al-Athar of Imam Muhammad.
4
See Imam Muhammad's adoption
Imam Muhammad quotes the athar and then states that they adopt the ruling: if the wife is adult and the husband minor, she gets maintenance. He attributes this to Abu Hanifa.
This confirms the position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Contrast with the opposite case
The text also notes: if the wife is young (saghira) and not capable of intercourse, she has no maintenance. This highlights that the determining factor is the wife's capability and surrender.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان الزوج صغيرا لا يقدر على الوطئ والمرأة كبيرة فلها النفقة من ماله

تشریح شوہر اتنا چھوٹا ہے کہ محبت پر قدرت نہیں رکھتا ہے اور بیوی بالغ ہے اور اپنے آپ کو سپرد کر چکی ہو تو اس کو شوہر کے مال سے نفقہ ملے گا۔ بیوی نے اپنے آپ کو سپرد کر دیا ہے اس لئے اس کو نفقہ ملے گا چاہے شوہر اس سے استفادہ نہ کر سکتا ہو۔ کیونکہ بیوی کی جانب سے احتباس ہو گیا ہے (۲) عن ابراهيم في الرجل يتزوج المرأة فلا يبنى بها قال : ان كان الحبس من قبل الرجل فعليه النفقة وان كان من قبل المرأة فلا نفقة لها، قال محمد و به ناخذ اذا كانت صغيرة لا تجامع مثلها فلا نفقة لها. وان كانت كبيرة والزوج صغير لا يجامع مثله فلها النفقة عليه في ماله وهو قول ابي حنيفة رحمة الله عليه (كتاب الآثار لامام محمد ، باب نفقته التي لم يدخل بها ص ۱۱۲ نمبر ۵۱۹)
And if the husband is young and unable to have intercourse, and the wife is adult, then she has maintenance from his wealth. [Urdu:] Explanation: The husband is so young that he has no power over intercourse, and the wife is adult and has surrendered herself, so she will receive maintenance from the husband's wealth. The wife has surrendered herself, so she will receive maintenance even if the husband cannot benefit from her, because ihtibas has occurred from the wife's side. (2) From Ibrahim regarding a man who marries a woman but does not consummate the marriage: he said, 'If the delay is from the man, then he is responsible for maintenance; if it is from the woman, then she has no maintenance.' Muhammad said: 'And we adopt: if she is young and not capable of intercourse, then she has no maintenance. If she is adult and the husband is young and not capable of intercourse, then she has maintenance from his wealth, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.' (Kitab al-Athar of Imam Muhammad, Chapter on Maintenance of the Woman with whom he has not Consummated, p. 112, no. 519)
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage deals with the opposite scenario of the previous lesson: here the husband is too young for intercourse, but the wife is adult and has surrendered. The ruling is that she is entitled to maintenance from the husband's property. The reason is that the wife has fulfilled her duty of ihtibas by surrendering herself, regardless of the husband's capability. The delay in consummation is due to the husband, so he must pay maintenance. The athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and the statement of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani confirm this as the position of Abu Hanifa. This shows that the Hanafi school focuses on the wife's action (ihtibas) rather than the husband's ability to take benefit. The athar also clarifies the distinction: if the wife is young, she gets no maintenance; if the husband is young and the wife adult, she does.

Key Terms
كبيرة (kabīrah): An adult wife who has reached the age where intercourse is possible and has surrendered herself.
حبس (ḥabs): Delay or confinement; here it refers to who is responsible for the lack of consummation (the husband or the wife).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on maintenance for an adult wife whose husband is a minor incapable of intercourse?
A) She has no maintenance because the husband cannot benefit.
B) She has maintenance from the husband's wealth because she surrendered.
C) She has maintenance only if she stays in her own home.
D) She has no maintenance until the husband reaches puberty.

Key Takeaway
An adult wife of a minor husband is entitled to maintenance because she has surrendered herself, regardless of the husband's inability to consummate.

Maintenance and Shelter for a Divorced Woman During Iddah
Ruling on Nafaqah and Sakan for Divorced Women in Iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance and shelter for a divorced woman during iddah and identify the Quranic and Hadith proofs for both revocable and irrevocable divorce.

Core Idea
A divorced woman, whether revocably or irrevocably, is entitled to maintenance and shelter during her iddah.

This lesson addresses a fundamental question in family law: what obligations does a husband have towards his divorced wife during her waiting period? The Hanafi school holds that maintenance (nafaqah) and shelter (sakan) are wajib for both revocable and irrevocable divorce, based on clear Quranic command and the practice of the Companions. We will examine the evidence and address the misconception arising from the hadith of Fatimah bint Qais.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (maintenance and shelter during iddah) and its ruling (wajib).
The ruling applies to both revocable (raj'i) and irrevocable (ba'in) divorce.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
Locate Surah al-Talaq 65:1, which commands not to expel divorced women from their homes.
The verse prohibits expulsion, implying the right to remain and be provided for.
3
Analyze the Quranic implication
Explain how the prohibition of expulsion directly implies the obligation of shelter and indirectly maintenance.
The Hanafi school derives both nafaqah and sakan from this verse.
4
Consider the Hadith evidence
Examine the hadith from Jabir where the Prophet explicitly grants shelter and maintenance to a woman divorced thrice.
This hadith reinforces the Quranic ruling and covers all types of divorce.
5
Address the counter-evidence
Discuss the hadith of Fatimah bint Qais and its rejection by the Hanafi school through Umar's statement.
Umar prioritized the Quran and Sunnah over an isolated ambiguous narration.

Source Text

واذا طلق الرجل امرأته فلها النفقة والسكنى في عدتها رجعيا كان او فائده

شوہر نے طلاق رجعی دی ہو یا بائنہ ، جب تک عدت گزار رہی ہو شوہر پر نفقہ اور سکنے لازم ہے۔ آیت میں ہے کہ مطلقہ عورت کو گھر سے نہ نکالوا بلکہ اس کو سکنی دو اور جب سکنی ہوگا تو تفقہ بھی ملے گا۔ یا ایھا النبي اذا طلقتم النساء فطلقوهن لعدتهن واحصوا العدة واتقوا الله ربكم لا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن ولا يخرجن ال ان يأتين بفاحشة مبينة (الف) ( آیت اسورہ الطلاق ۶۵) (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر عن النبي مال الله قال المطلقة ثلاثا لها السكني والنفقة (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب الطلاق ج رابع ص ۱۵ نمبر ۳۹۰۴) (۳) قال عمر لانترك كتاب الله وسنة نبينا لقول امرأة لا ندرى : لعلها حفظت او نسيت لها السكنى والنفقة وتلا الآية قال الله عز وجل لا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن ، سورة الطلاق آیت ا (ج) (مسلم شریف ، باب المطلقة البائن لا نفقة لهاص ۴۸۳ نمبر ۳۷۱۰/۱۴۸۰ را بو داؤد شریف، باب من انکر ذلک علی فاطمہ بنت قیس

حاشیہ: (الف) اے نبی ! اگر آپ گھورتوں کے طلاق دیں تو ان کی عدت کے موقع پر طلاق دیں اور عدت گئیں۔ اور اپنے رب اللہ سے تقوی اختیر کریں۔ ان کو گھروں سے نہ نکالیں اور وہ خود بھی نہ نکلیں مگر یہ کہ فاحشہ مہینہ کریں یعنی بدزبانی کرنے لگیں (ب) آپ نے فرمایا مطلقہ ثلاثہ کے لئے سکتے اور نفقہ ہے ( ج) حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ہم اللہ کی کتاب اور نبی کی سنت کو ایک عورت کی بات کی وجہ سے نہیں چھوڑ سکتے۔ معلوم نہیں اس نے یادر کھایا بھول گئی۔ اس کے لئے نفقہ اور سکنی ہے۔ پھر یہ آیت تلاوت کی کہ عورتوں کو ان کے گھروں سے نہ نکالو۔
And if a man divorces his wife, then she has maintenance and shelter during her iddah, whether the divorce is revocable or irrevocable. [Urdu:] Whether the husband gave a revocable or irrevocable divorce, as long as she is observing iddah, maintenance and shelter are obligatory upon the husband. The verse says: Do not expel the divorced women from their homes, rather give them shelter, and when there is shelter, maintenance will also be given. 'O Prophet, when you divorce women, divorce them for their iddah and count the iddah, and fear Allah your Lord. Do not expel them from their houses, nor should they leave unless they commit a clear immorality' (Surah al-Talaq 65:1) (a). (2) In the hadith: from Jabir from the Prophet, may Allah bless him, that he said: 'A woman divorced thrice has shelter and maintenance' (b) (Dar Qutni, Book of Divorce, Vol. 4, p. 15, no. 3904). (3) Umar said: 'We do not abandon the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of our Prophet for the statement of a woman; we do not know whether she remembered or forgot. She has shelter and maintenance.' Then he recited the verse: 'Do not expel them from their houses' (c) (Muslim, Chapter on the Irrevocably Divorced Woman has no Maintenance, p. 483, no. 3710/1480; Abu Dawud, Chapter on those who rejected that concerning Fatimah bint Qais). Footnotes: (a) O Prophet, if you divorce women, divorce them at the beginning of their iddah and count the iddah, and fear Allah your Lord. Do not expel them from their houses, nor should they leave unless they commit a clear immorality, i.e., become foul-mouthed. (b) He said: A woman divorced thrice has shelter and maintenance. (c) Umar said: We do not abandon the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of our Prophet for the statement of a woman; we do not know whether she remembered or forgot. She has shelter and maintenance. Then he recited this verse: 'Do not expel them from their houses.'
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage addresses a crucial point of fiqh: the right of a divorced woman to maintenance (nafaqah) and shelter (sakan) during her iddah (waiting period). The text explicitly states that this applies to both revocable (raj'i) and irrevocable (ba'in) divorce, countering the misunderstanding that an irrevocably divorced woman has no claim. The proof is drawn from the Quranic verse (65:1) commanding that women not be expelled from their homes during iddah, which implies they must be provided for. Additionally, the hadith from Jabir and the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab reinforce this. Umar's statement is particularly significant: he rejected the isolated hadith of Fatimah bint Qais (which said an irrevocably divorced woman has no maintenance) because it contradicted the general principle of the Quran and Sunnah. This shows that in the Hanafi school, the general principle takes precedence over a specific ambiguous narration.

Key Terms
عدة (‘iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before she can remarry.
سكنى (suknā): Shelter or housing provided for the divorced woman during her iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of divorced woman is entitled to maintenance and shelter during her iddah?
A) Only the revocably divorced woman.
B) Only the irrevocably divorced woman.
C) Both revocably and irrevocably divorced women.
D) Only women divorced before consummation.

Key Takeaway
A divorced woman's right to maintenance and shelter during her iddah is a confirmed obligation in the Hanafi school, regardless of the type of divorce, based on the Quran and the authentic practice of the Companions.

Nafaqah — Maintenance

Maintenance for Wife with Minor Husband
Ruling on nafaqah when husband is minor and wife adult

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance for an adult wife of a minor husband, identify the condition of ihtibas, and explain the proof from hadith and the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Core Idea
Maintenance is due from a minor husband if the adult wife surrenders herself (ihtibas).

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: an adult woman married to a minor boy who cannot consummate the marriage. The Hanafi school rules that she is entitled to maintenance from his wealth if she has surrendered herself to his authority. This ruling is derived from the general command in the hadith and the principle that maintenance is tied to the wife's confinement, not the husband's ability to benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The act is maintenance (nafaqah) for a wife. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) when the wife is adult and the husband is minor, provided she has surrendered (ihtibas).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Muslim: 'Wa lahuuna 'alaykum rizquhunna wa kiswatuhunna bil ma'ruf' and the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i as recorded in Kitab al-Athar.
The hadith is general and does not distinguish between types of wives.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses a general command (al-amr) which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (wujub). The phrase does not exclude any type of wife, so it includes adult wives of minor husbands.
The command 'lahunna' is an imperative, indicating obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad initially held that a wife who cannot engage in intercourse (due to her being minor) gets no maintenance, but for the case of an adult wife with a minor husband, he adopts Abu Hanifa's view: she gets maintenance because she has surrendered.
The difference is based on who causes the 'restriction' (habs).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that maintenance is due. Imam Muhammad says 'wa bihi na'khudh' for this ruling, indicating it is the school's adopted view.
The tarjih authority is Imam Muhammad himself in Kitab al-Athar.

[2133](2) And if the husband is young, unable to have intercourse, and the woman is adult, then she has the right to maintenance from his wealth. [2134] And if a man divorces his wife, then she has the right to maintenance and housing during her waiting period, whether it is a revocable or an irrevocable divorce. Imam Shafi'i said: because the woman has gone to the husband's house and has surrendered herself, so apparently confinement has occurred, therefore even if he cannot benefit from her, she still has maintenance. Hadith: 'And for them (wives) upon you is their provision and clothing according to what is reasonable' (Muslim Sharif no. 1218). In it, no distinction is made between an adult and a minor wife; rather, maintenance is obligatory for every type of wife. Therefore maintenance is also for a minor wife. [2133] (6) And if the husband is young, unable to have intercourse, and the woman is adult, then she has maintenance from the husband's wealth. Explanation: The husband is so young that he is unable to have intercourse, and the wife is adult and has surrendered herself; then she will receive maintenance from the husband's wealth. She has surrendered herself, so she receives maintenance even if the husband cannot benefit from her, because confinement has occurred from the wife's side. (2) From Ibrahim regarding a man who marries a woman but does not consummate the marriage; he said: If the restriction is from the man, then he must provide maintenance; if it is from the woman, then no maintenance for her. Muhammad said: And we adopt this: if she is young and cannot engage in intercourse like her, then no maintenance for her. And if she is an adult and the husband is young and cannot engage in intercourse like him, then she has maintenance from his wealth, and this is the statement of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. (Kitab al-Athar of Imam Muhammad, chapter on maintenance of one not consummated, p. 112 no. 519)
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage type is a ruling with proof. It establishes that an adult wife is entitled to maintenance from her minor husband's wealth even if he cannot consummate the marriage, provided she has surrendered herself to him (tamkin/ihitibas). The key principle is that maintenance is linked to the wife's confinement (ihitibas), not the husband's actual benefit. The Hanafi school relies on the general command of the Quran ('wa lahuuna' hadith) and the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, as transmitted by Imam Muhammad in Kitab al-Athar. The ruling distinguishes: if the wife is minor and cannot engage in intercourse, she gets no maintenance; but if she is adult and the husband is minor, she does. This is the position of Abu Hanifa, and it is the relied-upon view. The proof is the hadith which does not differentiate between adult and minor wives.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance/expenses the husband must provide to his wife, including food, clothing, and lodging.
الاحتباس (al-ihtibas): The wife's confinement/surrender of herself to the husband's authority, making her available for marital relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the marriage contract alone obligates maintenance.
B) Because the wife has surrendered herself (ihtibas), making her eligible.
C) Because the husband has the financial ability.
D) Because the minor husband is legally considered capable of providing benefit.

Key Takeaway
An adult wife's maintenance from a minor husband is wajib if she surrenders herself (ihtibas), regardless of his inability to consummate.

No Maintenance for Widow during Iddah
Ruling with proof: Widow has no nafaqah during iddah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance for a widow during her iddah and explain the two rational proofs (naql and aql) that support it.

Core Idea
A widow's iddah is an act of worship, not a service to the husband, so no maintenance is due from his estate.

This lesson addresses a specific Hanafi ruling: a woman whose husband has died and is observing iddah is not entitled to maintenance from his estate. While one might assume that any iddah entails maintenance, the Hanafi school distinguishes the widow's iddah from that of a divorced woman. The reasoning is both textual and analogical, rooted in the nature of the obligation and the ownership of the deceased's wealth. By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise legal basis for this ruling and be able to apply it in real scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
Note the specific subject: a woman whose husband has died (al-mutawaffa 'anha zawjuha). The ruling is explicitly 'no maintenance' (la nafqah). This is a negative ruling—an absence of obligation.
The ruling is categorical; there are no exceptions mentioned in the source.
2
Locate the two reasons
The text gives two distinct rationales: first, the widow's iddah is an act of worship (ibadah) for Allah, not a right of the husband; second, after death, the husband's wealth belongs to his heirs, and it is not permissible to obligate maintenance from others' property.
Both reasons are independently sufficient; together they reinforce the ruling.
3
Compare with divorced woman's iddah
The text contrasts the widow with a divorced woman whose iddah is for the husband's right (to know about pregnancy). That type of iddah generates maintenance. The widow's iddah does not serve a spousal right.
This comparison highlights the key distinction: the purpose of the iddah determines the financial obligation.
4
Examine the proof structure
The Hanafi proof is a rational argument (qiyas) based on two premises: the nature of the iddah as ibadah, and the transfer of ownership upon death. These are considered decisive proofs (qati' al-dalalah).
No explicit Quranic or hadith text is cited for this specific ruling; the proof is purely rational.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
Consider a widow named Fatima. She is in her four-month-ten-day iddah. Her husband left a house and cash. According to this ruling, she cannot demand maintenance from the estate beyond her inheritance share. She must support herself or rely on her family.
The practical consequence is that the widow's financial situation during iddah is not guaranteed by the deceased's estate.

(4) The woman observing iddah does so for the husband to know if there is pregnancy; therefore maintenance is obligatory on the husband. The ba'in divorced woman is not a wife in any sense, and there is no child of the husband in her womb, so she has no maintenance. (2) In the hadith: the long hadith of Fatimah bint Qays, in which she was not given maintenance or housing. [2135] (8) And there is no maintenance for a woman whose husband has died. Explanation: A woman whose husband has died and who is observing iddah has no maintenance. There is no maintenance because the woman's observance of iddah is not for the right of the husband, but for a legal right that is considered an act of worship. This is why the iddah of a woman whose husband has died is not by menstruation but by counting days: four months and ten days, whether she menstruates or not. (2) After the husband's death, the wealth he leaves no longer belongs to him; rather, it becomes the property of others (the heirs). And it is not permissible to prescribe maintenance for anyone from the wealth of others.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage type is a ruling with proof. It states that a widow (mutawaffa 'anha zawjuha) is not entitled to maintenance from the deceased husband's estate during her iddah. The reasoning is twofold: first, the widow's iddah is an obligation from Allah (ibadah), not a right of the husband, so it does not obligate maintenance; second, after death, the husband's wealth passes to his heirs and cannot be encumbered by a new obligation. This is different from a divorced woman whose iddah is for the husband's right to know about pregnancy, so maintenance is due. The text also notes the Shafi'i position on ba'in divorce, but that is a tangent. The Hanafi ruling is clear: a widow gets no nafaqah.

Key Terms
المتوفى عنها زوجها (al-mutawaffa 'anha zawjuha): A woman whose husband has died; a widow.
العدة (al-'iddah): Waiting period; for a widow, it is specific duration for certainty of non-pregnancy.

D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
A widow's iddah is a religious observance, not a marital service, so she has no claim to maintenance from the deceased husband's estate.

No Maintenance for Wife When Separation Is Due to Her Disobedience
Ruling that maintenance is forfeited when separation results from wife's sin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a wife forfeits maintenance during iddah when separation is due to her disobedience, and identify the proof (dalil) from the athar of Fatimah bint Qays.

Core Idea
Separation caused by the wife's sin nullifies her right to nafaqah.

In Hanafi law, the right to maintenance during the waiting period (iddah) is not absolute. When a marriage ends due to the wife's disobedience or sin, she loses her entitlement. This lesson examines the textual proofs from the Companions that establish this exception, focusing on the case of Fatimah bint Qays and the general principle that fault determines maintenance rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first sentence: 'Every separation that comes from the woman due to disobedience, then there is no maintenance for her.' This is the general rule.
The ruling applies to any separation (talaq, khula, annulment) caused by the wife's fault.
2
Locate the primary proof
The text cites the athar from Sulayman ibn Yasar about Fatimah bint Qays: her separation was due to 'bad character' and she received no maintenance.
This athar is from Abu Dawud and is considered zanni al-thubut.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'due to bad character' explicitly links the cause (disobedience) to the consequence (loss of maintenance). This is the key link.
Hanafi usul uses this to establish causation: the wife's sin abrogates her right.
4
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Some madhahib may distinguish between types of sin or separation. The Hanafi school applies the rule uniformly when the wife is at fault.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Apply to a scenario
Test the ruling: if a wife commits nushuz leading to khula, she gets no maintenance. If the husband divorces for no fault of hers, she does.
The decisive factor is the origin of the separation.

Source Text

[2136] (9) And every separation that comes from the woman due to disobedience, then there is no maintenance for her. If the separation occurred due to the woman's fault and disobedience, then she will not receive maintenance. Because the separation was due to the woman's disobedience, not the husband's mischief, therefore she will not receive maintenance during iddah. Commentary
This passage type is a ruling with proof. It establishes that if a separation (such as annulment or irrevocable divorce) occurs due to the wife's disobedience or sin (ma'siyah), she is not entitled to maintenance during her iddah. The principle is that the right to maintenance is tied to the wife's obedience and surrender; if she is the cause of the breakdown, she forfeits that right. The text cites the example of Fatimah bint Qays, whose separation was due to her bad character (su' al-khuluq), and athars from Sulayman ibn Yasar and 'Amir support this. This ruling applies to any separation that originates from the wife's fault.

المعصية (al-ma'siyah): Disobedience/sin by the wife that leads to the dissolution of marriage.
الفرقة (al-furqah): Separation/divorce or annulment between spouses.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Maintenance for Widow in 'Iddah
Ruling with proof on widow's maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance for a widow during 'iddah and explain the reasoning that distinguishes her case from that of a revocably divorced woman.

Core Idea
A widow's 'iddah is an act of worship, not a spousal right, so no maintenance is due.

When a woman's husband dies, she must observe a waiting period ('iddah) of four months and ten days. A key question is whether she is entitled to maintenance (nafaqah) from her husband's estate during this period. This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling, which is that a widow receives no maintenance because her 'iddah is a religious obligation (ta'abbudi) rather than a period to ascertain paternity. It also compares this ruling with the Shafi'i position, which extends the denial of maintenance to all irrevocably divorced women.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify that the ruling is specific to a widow (mutawaffa 'anha zawjuha) and that she has no maintenance during her 'iddah. Contrast with the revocably divorced woman who does have maintenance.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that the widow's 'iddah is not due to the husband's right but is a purely religious duty. Therefore, maintenance is not obligatory because the wife is not observing 'iddah for the husband's sake.
The text also notes that after death, the husband's property passes to heirs, and one cannot impose maintenance from the wealth of others.
3
Examine the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i, citing the hadith of Fatima bint Qais, argues that no maintenance is due for any woman in bain (irrevocable) divorce, including widows. The Hanafi school limits this hadith to cases where the separation is due to the woman's fault.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by distinguishing the cause of 'iddah: the widow's 'iddah is ta'abbudi, not for the husband's benefit. Additionally, the hadith may be specific to Fatima's situation, where she was at fault.
This is a classic case of takhsis (limitation) of a general text.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is that under Hanafi law, a widow receives no maintenance, while under Shafi'i law, she also receives none. However, the reasoning differs, affecting cases like bain divorce where the woman is not at fault.
In later Hanafi practice, some exceptions exist for bain divorce caused by the husband's fault, but the widow's case remains clear.

Source Text

بائنا [2135] (۸) ولا نفقة للمتوفى عنها زوجها (۱۳۶ (۹) وكل فرقة جائت من قبل المرأة بمعصية فلا نفقة لها.

Bain [2135] (8) And there is no maintenance for the one whose husband has died. (136 (9) And every separation that comes from the woman's side due to sin, there is no maintenance for her. From hadith and athar it became known that for a woman observing 'iddah there is maintenance and lodging. The woman in 'iddah is observing 'iddah for the husband so that it becomes known whether there is a child in the womb or not, therefore maintenance is obligatory on the husband. Imam Shafi'i says that there is no maintenance for the woman of bain divorce. The woman of bain divorce is in no way a wife, and there is no child of the husband in her womb, therefore there is no maintenance for her. There is a hadith: the long hadith of Fatima bint Qais in which she was not given maintenance or lodging. From Fatima bint Qais... she said: I mentioned that to the Messenger of Allah and he said: 'No maintenance for you and no lodging.' (Muslim, Bab al-Mutallaqah al-Ba'in la Nafqata laha, p. 483, no. 148; Abu Dawud, Bab fi Nafqat al-Subut, p. 1319, no. 2284) From this hadith it became known that for the woman of bain separation there is no maintenance and no lodging. [2135] (8) And there is no maintenance for the one whose husband has died. Explanation: The woman whose husband has died and she is observing 'iddah, there is no maintenance for her. The reason for no maintenance is that the woman's observing 'iddah is not due to the husband's right but due to a shari' right which is counted as worship. And this is the reason that the 'iddah of a widow is not by menses but by counting days: four months and ten days, whether she menstruates or not. (2) After the husband's death, the wealth he left does not remain in his ownership but becomes that of others (heirs). And imposing maintenance in the wealth of others is not permissible.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (hukm) on maintenance (nafaqah) for a widow during her 'iddah (waiting period). The text first quotes the matn: 'There is no maintenance for the one whose husband has died.' Then the commentator explains the reasoning. The key point is that the widow's 'iddah is not for the benefit of the husband (to ascertain paternity) but is a purely religious obligation (ta'abbudi). Therefore, unlike a divorced woman in revocable divorce, maintenance is not obligatory on the husband's estate because the 'iddah is not a right of the husband. The commentator also contrasts this with the case of bain (irrevocable) divorce, citing the hadith of Fatima bint Qais where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled no maintenance or lodging. Imam Shafi'i uses this hadith to deny maintenance for all bain divorced women. The Hanafi position distinguishes: for a widow, maintenance is not due; for a bain divorced woman, the Hanafi school also says no maintenance (though some exceptions exist in later fiqh). The commentator clarifies that after death, the husband's property passes to heirs, and obligating maintenance from their wealth is not permissible. The hadith and athar mentioned earlier (reference to p. 1320) establish that a woman in revocable 'iddah does get maintenance, but the widow's case is different because her 'iddah is a religious duty, not a spousal right.

Key Terms
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and lodging, that a husband is obligated to provide to his wife during marriage and for certain periods after separation.
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after the death of her husband or after divorce, during which she cannot remarry.
بائنہ طلاق (bain talaq): Irrevocable divorce; the marriage is permanently ended unless a new marriage contract is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the husband's wealth is not enough
D) Because she is in bain divorce

Key Takeaway
A widow's 'iddah is a religious duty, not a spousal right, so she is not entitled to maintenance in Hanafi fiqh.
