Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
9 min
No Maintenance When Separation Is Due to Woman's Sin
Ruling with proof: 'iddah maintenance drops when woman's sin causes separation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on dropping 'iddah maintenance due to the woman's sin, identify the proofs, and apply the exception for disobedience to obtain a legitimate right.

Core Idea
If separation is the woman's fault, she loses 'iddah maintenance; if she disobeys to claim a right, she keeps it.

This lesson unpacks a crucial Hanafi rule: a woman undergoing 'iddah (waiting period) normally receives maintenance from her husband, but this right drops if the marriage dissolved due to her sin or disobedience. We will examine the textual proofs from the case of Fatima bint Qais and the reports of Sulayman ibn Yasar and 'Amir, then explore the important exception: disobedience to obtain a legitimate right does not forfeit maintenance. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion between different types of separations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is 'iddah maintenance (nafaqah) for a woman after separation. The ruling: generally wajib (obligatory), but the clause in the matn states that if the separation comes from the woman's side due to sin, she has no maintenance.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on the cause of separation.
2
Locate the dalil
The narrator cites the case of Fatima bint Qais (marfu' hadith) and two athar from Sulayman ibn Yasar and 'Amir. The first athar explains that Fatima's loss of maintenance was due to her bad character (sū' al-khuluq). The second athar states a husband is not obliged to spend if the wife is imprisoned due to her own fault.
These are considered supporting evidence (shawahid) for the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these proofs establish the ruling? The hadith of Fatima bint Qais is general: the Prophet said no maintenance or lodging. The additional explanation from Sulayman ibn Yasar and 'Amir links the loss of maintenance specifically to the woman's bad character or fault. Thus, the cause (illah) is the woman's sin causing separation.
The Hanafi school derives the rule that maintenance drops when the woman is at fault.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position is distinct from the Shafi'i view. Imam Shafi'i generally holds that a woman divorced with a bain divorce (irrevocable) receives no maintenance regardless of fault, based on a literal reading of the Hadith of Fatima. The Hanafi school restricts it to fault-based separations, using the additional athar to clarify the 'illah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fih).
5
Evaluate the tarjih and exception
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that if the woman's sin caused the separation, no nafaqah. However, an important qualification is added: if the disobedience is to obtain a legitimate right (e.g., seeking khul' due to husband's harm), maintenance does not drop. This shows the principle is not punitive but based on causation.
The exception is derived from the broader Hanafi maxim that rights are not lost by exercising one's rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[2136] (۹) وكل فرقة جائت من قبل المرأة بمعصية فلا نفقة لها.
عورت کی غلطی اور اس کی معصیت کی بنا پر تفریق ہوئی تو عورت کو نفقہ نہیں ملے گا۔
چونکہ عورت کی نافرمانی کی وجہ سے فرقت ہوئی ہے، شوہر کی شرارت نہیں ہے اس لئے عورت کو عدت کا نفقہ نہیں ملے گا (۲) فاطمہ بنت قیس کی نافرمانی تھی اس لئے اس کو نفقہ اور سکنی نہیں ملا۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن سلیمان بن یسار في خروج فاطمة قال انما كان ذلك من سوء الخلق (ب) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب من انکر ذلک علی فاطمہ بنت قیس ص ۳۲۰ نمبر ۲۲۹۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کی نافرمانی ہو جس کی وجہ سے تفریق ہوئی ہو تو اس کو نفقہ نہیں ملے گا۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن عامر قال ليس للرجل ان ينفق على امرأته اذا كان بالحبس من قبلها (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی هیبتة ۱۹۹ ما قالوافي الرجل يتزوج المرأة تطلب النفقة قبل ان يدخل بها هل لها ذلك؟ ج رابع ، حاشیه : (الف) حضرت فاطمہ بنت قیس فرماتی ہے کہ میں اس کا تذکرہ ( یعنی طلاق بائنہ کا تذکرہ) حضور کے سامنے کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا تیرے لئے نہ نفقہ ہے اور نہ سکتے ہے (ب) سلیمان بن یسار حضرت فاطمہ کے گھر سے نکلنے کے بارے میں فرماتے ہیں کہ بدزبانی کی وجہ سے ہوا ہے ( ج ) حضرت عامر فرماتے ہیں کہ شوہر پر ضروری نہیں ہے کہ بیوی کو نفقہ دے جبکہ قید خود اس کی وجہ سے ہو۔
لیکن کسی حق کو وصول کرنے کے لئے نافرمانی ہو تو نفقہ ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔
[2136] (9) And every separation that comes from the woman's side due to sin, she has no maintenance. If separation occurs due to the woman's fault and her sin, she will not receive maintenance. Since the separation happened due to the woman's disobedience, not the husband's mischief, therefore she will not receive 'iddah maintenance. (2) Fatima bint Qais was disobedient, therefore she did not get maintenance or lodging. There is an athar: from Sulayman ibn Yasar regarding Fatima's leaving: 'That was only due to bad character.' (Abu Dawud, Bab man ankara dhalika 'ala Fatima, p. 320, no. 2294) From this athar it is known that if the woman's disobedience caused the separation, she will not get maintenance. There is an athar: from 'Amir: 'It is not necessary for the husband to spend on his wife when the imprisonment is due to her.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 199, 'Ma qalu fi al-rajul...') Footnote: (a) Fatima bint Qais said: I mentioned that (i.e., the bain divorce) to the Prophet and he said: 'No maintenance for you and no lodging.' (b) Sulayman ibn Yasar says about Fatima's leaving: it was due to bad language. (c) 'Amir says: It is not necessary for the husband to give maintenance when the confinement is due to her. However, if the disobedience is to obtain a right, maintenance does not drop.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This is a ruling (hukm) about the condition for dropping 'iddah maintenance. The matn states: 'Every separation that comes from the woman's side due to sin, she has no maintenance.' The commentator explains the general principle: if the separation (firqah) occurs because of the woman's sin or disobedience (ma'siyah), she loses her right to nafaqah during the 'iddah. The reason is that the separation is caused by her, not by the husband's wrongdoing. The commentator cites the case of Fatima bint Qais: her separation was due to her bad character, so the Prophet denied her maintenance. Two athar (reports from Companions/Successors) support this: (1) Sulayman ibn Yasar attributes Fatima's leaving to bad character; (2) 'Amir states that a husband is not obliged to spend if the wife is imprisoned due to her own fault. Then an important qualification is added: 'However, if the disobedience is to obtain a right, maintenance does not drop.' So if the woman disobeys to claim a legitimate right (like khul' or seeking justice), she does not lose her nafaqah. This is a key nuance.

Key Terms
معصیت (ma'siyah): Sin or disobedience; in this context, any act of the woman that causes the dissolution of the marriage or separation due to her fault.
فرقت/تفریق (firqah / tafriq): Separation between spouses, whether by divorce, annulment, or death.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance; financial support that a husband must provide to his wife during marriage and during the 'iddah period.
عدت ('iddah): Waiting period after divorce or death of husband during which a woman cannot remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) She apostates from Islam
C) She disobeys to obtain a legitimate right
D) She commits adultery

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditions the obligation of 'iddah maintenance on the cause of separation: if the woman's sin caused it, no maintenance; otherwise, it remains wajib.

Apostasy After Divorce Drops 'Iddah Maintenance
Ruling that apostasy after divorce cancels 'iddah maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'iddah maintenance when a divorced woman apostates and explain the two legal rationales given in the text.

Core Idea
A divorced woman's apostasy during 'iddah forfeits her maintenance: disobedience and kufr sever the right.

This lesson examines a specific sub-ruling from the chapter on nafaqah: what happens to a divorcée's 'iddah maintenance if she leaves Islam after the divorce? The Hanafi school holds that her apostasy cancels the maintenance entirely, based on two clear legal rationales. Understanding this ruling requires connecting two core principles: first, that a woman at fault loses her nafaqah; second, that nafaqah is a right prescribed for Muslim spouses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State clearly what the text rules: a divorced woman's apostasy during 'iddah drops her right to nafaqah (maintenance).
The ruling applies even though the divorce preceded the apostasy.
2
Extract the first rationale
The text says apostasy is an act of disobedience (ma'siyah) from the woman's side, and as established earlier, a wife who disobeys loses her nafaqah.
This links to the general principle that nafaqah is forfeited by the wife's fault.
3
Extract the second rationale
The text also argues that nafaqah is given only to a Muslim woman, and an apostate is a non-Muslim, so she cannot receive it from a Muslim husband.
This is a rational (aql) argument based on the nature of the right.
4
Synthesize the two reasons
Both reasons independently justify the dropping of maintenance. They are complementary: one based on the woman's action, the other on her status.
The two reasons together reinforce the ruling.

(2137) (10) And if he divorces her then she apostates, her maintenance drops. If a woman is divorced then she becomes an apostate, her maintenance will drop. It has passed earlier that if disobedience occurs from the woman's side, she does not get maintenance, and here she has disobeyed by apostasy, therefore she will not get maintenance. (2) Maintenance is given to a Muslim woman, and she has become an infidel, so how can she get maintenance?
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This is a ruling (hukm) expanding on the previous principle. If a woman receives a (revocable) divorce and then apostates from Islam during her 'iddah, her right to nafaqah drops. Two reasons are given: (1) Apostasy is an act of disobedience (ma'siyah) from the woman's side, and as established in the previous ruling, any separation due to her sin forfeits nafaqah. (2) Nafaqah is a right that Allah prescribes for Muslim wives; an apostate woman is not a Muslim, so she is not entitled to nafaqah from a Muslim husband. This ruling applies even though the divorce was issued before the apostasy. The logic is consistent with the overall principle that maintenance during 'iddah is linked to the woman being a Muslim and not being at fault.

Key Terms
ارتدت (irtaddat): She apostates; a married woman leaving Islam, which severs the marriage contract.

Maintenance and Adultery with Step-Son: The Timing of the Act
Ruling with causal analysis (ta'lil) on nafaqah in a specific adultery case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'iddah maintenance when a woman commits adultery with her stepson, and explain how the timing of the act relative to the divorce determines the outcome.

Core Idea
Maintenance drops only when the woman's sin directly caused the separation.

This lesson examines a specific edge case in Hanafi family law: a woman who has sexual relations with her stepson. The ruling on her 'iddah maintenance hinges entirely on whether that act occurred before or after the divorce. The key principle is that maintenance is forfeited only when the wife's disobedience is the direct cause of the marital dissolution. We will walk through the reasoning (ta'lil) and the distinction drawn by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the two scenarios: adultery before divorce vs. after divorce, and the maintenance consequence for each.
The ruling is a conditional: if after → nafaqah; if before → no nafaqah.
2
Understand the causal analysis
Analyze why the timing matters. The divorce itself is the legal separation. If the adultery occurs after an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain), the separation is already complete; the adultery did not cause it. If the adultery occurs before, it likely caused the divorce (or was the reason for the dissolution), so the woman's disobedience is the cause.
The commentary emphasizes 'sabab' (cause).
3
Recognize the principle of disobedience
In Hanafi law, a wife who is disobedient (nashiz) loses her right to maintenance. Here, the adultery is an act of disobedience, but its effect on maintenance depends on whether it caused the separation.
The text cites the athar (Fatima bint Qais) to support that disobedience leads to loss of nafaqah.
4
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Consider a case where the woman commits adultery after the divorce but before the 'iddah ends. She has sinned but the separation was already caused by the divorce. Therefore, she still gets maintenance.

اگر عورت نے شوہر کے بیٹے کو قدرت دی اپنی ذات پر پس اگر طلاق کے بعد ہو تو عورت کے لئے نفقہ ہوگا اور اگر طلاق سے پہلے ہے تو اس کے لئے نفقہ نہیں ہے۔

طلاق کے بعد صحبت کرائی تو صحبت کرانے سے تفریق نہیں ہوئی بلکہ طلاق بائنہ واقع ہونے سے تفریق ہو چکی ہے اور وہ عدت گزار رہی ہے اس لئے سوتیلے بیٹے سے زنا کرانا گناہ ضرور ہے لیکن چونکہ یہ تفریق کا سبب نہیں ہے اس لئے نفقہ ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کی نافرمانی نہیں ہوئی۔
اور اگر طلاق سے پہلے شوہر کے بیٹے سے صحبت کرائی تو اس کو نفقہ نہیں ملے گا۔
طلاق سے پہلے سوتیلے بیٹے سے صحبت کرائی اس لئے صحبت کی وجہ سے نکاح ٹوٹا اور وہ تفریق کا سبب بنا اور عی عورت کی نافرمانی اور معصیت کی وجہ سے ہے اس لئے عورت کو عدت کا نفقہ نہیں ملے گا (۲) اس کے لئے اثر او پر گزر چکا ہے۔ قال انما كان ذلك من سوء الخلق ( ابوداؤد شریف نمبر ۲۲۹۴)
[2138] (11) And if she enables her husband's son over herself, then if it is after divorce, she has maintenance, and if it is before divorce, she has no maintenance. If the woman gives her husband's son power over herself, then if it is after divorce, she will have maintenance, and if it is before divorce, she will have no maintenance. Explanation: The husband had a son from another wife; the woman committed adultery with him. If she did it after the bain divorce, she will get maintenance. If she did it before divorce, which caused the separation, she will not get maintenance. If she did it after divorce, the separation was not caused by the adultery but by the previous bain divorce; she is observing 'iddah, so even though committing adultery with the stepson is a sin, because it was not the cause of separation, her maintenance does not drop, because she was not disobedient (in that regard). And if she did it before divorce, the marriage was broken by the adultery, which became the cause of separation, and due to the woman's disobedience and sin, she will not get 'iddah maintenance. The athar for this has already passed: 'That was only due to bad character.' (Abu Dawud, no. 2294)
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This ruling (hukm) addresses a specific scenario: a woman who commits adultery with her stepson (her husband's son from another wife). The key is the timing relative to the divorce. If the adultery occurred after the (irrevocable) divorce has already taken place, the separation (firqah) was not caused by her act; it was caused by the husband's divorce. Therefore, although she has sinned, she is not considered 'disobedient' in the sense of causing the separation, so she retains her right to 'iddah maintenance. However, if the adultery occurred before the divorce and was the cause of the dissolution of the marriage (i.e., the husband divorced her because of it, or the marriage was annulled), then the separation is due to her sin and she forfeits maintenance. The text emphasizes the causal link: maintenance drops only when the woman's sin is the direct cause of the separation. The athar of Fatima bint Qais is cited again to support the principle that disobedience leads to loss of nafaqah.

Key Terms
مگنت (makkanat): She enabled or allowed; in this context, she voluntarily had sexual intercourse with her stepson.
سبب (sabab): Cause or reason; here, the cause of the separation determines maintenance rights.
نفاقه (nafaqah): Maintenance, financial support due to a wife during marriage and 'iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi ruling, when does a woman who commits adultery with her stepson still receive 'iddah maintenance?
A) If she committed adultery before the divorce
B) If she committed adultery after the divorce
C) She never receives maintenance
D) She always receives maintenance

Key Takeaway
Maintenance during 'iddah is forfeited only when the woman's disobedience is the direct cause of the marital separation.

Principle: 'Iddah Maintenance Only for Revocably Divorced Women
Summary principle with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle regarding 'iddah maintenance and identify which divorced women are entitled to nafaqah.

Core Idea
Only a revocably divorced woman (raj'i) receives 'iddah maintenance; an irrevocably divorced woman does not.

This passage summarizes the overarching principle that governs 'iddah maintenance in the Hanafi school. It distinguishes between separation caused by the woman's fault and by the man's initiative, and provides a hadith to support the rule. Understanding this principle is key to correctly applying nafaqah rulings in various divorce scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Read the first sentence: 'All these issues are based on this principle: that if the separation occurred due to a fault from the woman's side... then she will not get maintenance.' State the principle in your own words.
The principle is a conditional rule: woman's fault → no nafaqah; man's fault → nafaqah.
2
Examine the Hadith Proof
Read the hadith: 'The woman divorced three times has no lodging and no maintenance; lodging and maintenance are only for the one who has the right of return.' Identify the key phrase that limits entitlement.
The phrase 'liman yamlik al-raj'a' is the core indicator.
3
Apply to a Case
Consider a woman who is divorced for the first time (revocable) versus a woman divorced for the third time (irrevocable). Based on the principle and hadith, determine who receives nafaqah.
4
Note the Scope
The principle also covers cases where separation is due to the woman's sin (e.g., apostasy, adultery). Understand that the same rule applies: if the separation is final and due to her fault, no maintenance.
This is an extension of the principle beyond divorce to other forms of separation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول یہ سب مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ عورت کی جانب سے غلطی کی وجہ سے تفریق ہوئی ہو یا احتباس نہ ہوا ہو تو عورت کو نفقہ نہیں ملے گا۔ اور مرد کی جانب سے طلاق ہوئی ہو تو نفقہ ملے گا۔ اس حدیث سے اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ عن عامر عن فاطمة بنت قيس قالت قال رسول الله الله المطلقة ثلاثا لاسكنى لها ولا نفقة انما السكنى والنفقة لمن يملك الرجعة (الف) (دارقطنی، کتاب الطلاق ج رابع ص ۱۵ نمبر ۳۹۰۷) اس حدیث سے تو پتہ چلتا ہے کہ رجعی طلاق والی کے علاوہ کسی کو عدت کا نفقہ نہیں ملے گا۔ اس لئے جن صورتوں میں عورت کی جانب سے نافرمانی ہو ان صورتوں میں عورت کو نفقہ نہیں ملے گا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کہ مطلقہ ثلاثہ کونہ سکنے ملے گا اور نہ نفقہ ملے گا۔ سکنی اور نفقہ اس کے لے ہے جس کو طلاق رجعی دی ہو۔
Principle: All these issues are based on this principle: that if the separation occurred due to a fault from the woman's side or if there was no restraint (i.e., she was not imprisoned wrongfully), then she will not get maintenance. And if the divorce came from the man's side, she will get maintenance. The following hadith supports this: From 'Amir from Fatima bint Qais who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The woman divorced three times has no lodging and no maintenance; lodging and maintenance are only for the one who has the right of return (raj'a).' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Talaq, vol. 4, p. 15, no. 3907) This hadith shows that no one other than the revocably divorced woman gets 'iddah maintenance. Therefore, in cases where the woman's disobedience is present, she will not get maintenance. Footnote: (a) He said: A woman divorced three times has no lodging and no maintenance; lodging and maintenance are for the one given a revocable divorce.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This is a concluding principle (usul) summarizing the rulings presented above. The commentator states that all the previous cases (widow, separation due to woman's sin, apostasy, stepson adultery) follow one consistent rule: if the separation is caused by the woman's fault or if she is not wrongfully confined (possibly referring to the hadith of 'imprisonment'), she loses her 'iddah maintenance. Conversely, if the divorce is initiated by the husband (and not due to her fault), she retains nafaqah. The commentator then cites a hadith from Darqutni: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that a woman divorced three times (i.e., irrevocably) has no lodging or maintenance; only the woman in a revocable divorce (raj'i) is entitled. This hadith is used as a proof that maintenance during 'iddah is not for all women, but only for those where the marriage could potentially be restored (i.e., the husband retains the right to take her back). Thus, the principle is that when the separation is final and due to the woman's wrongdoing, no maintenance is due. The footnote reinforces this: the triply divorced woman (mujallalah) gets nothing.

Key Terms
رجعت/رجعی (raj'a / raj'i): Revocable divorce; a divorce where the husband can take his wife back without a new marriage contract during the 'iddah.
مطلقہ ثلاثہ (mutallaqah thalathah): Woman divorced three times (irrevocably); she cannot be taken back unless she marries someone else and is divorced.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance, financial support during the 'iddah period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle stated in this passage, who is entitled to 'iddah maintenance and lodging?
A) Any woman who is divorced
B) Only a widow
C) Only a woman in revocable divorce (raj'i)
D) Only a woman divorced three times

Key Takeaway
The sole determinant for 'iddah maintenance is whether the husband retains the right to take his wife back during the 'iddah; if the divorce is irrevocable (bain) or due to the woman's fault, no maintenance is due.

Maintenance for an Apostate Wife After Divorce
Ruling on maintenance after apostasy following divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance when a wife apostatizes after divorce and explain the two underlying rationales: nushuz and the prohibition of maintaining a non-Muslim.

Core Idea
Apostasy after divorce cancels maintenance – it is nushuz and a Muslim cannot support a non-Muslim.

This lesson unpacks a concise ruling from the Hanafi matn: if a husband divorces his wife and she subsequently leaves Islam, her right to post-divorce maintenance (nafaqah) immediately ceases. The ruling rests on two principles: apostasy constitutes extreme disobedience (nushuz), and a Muslim husband is not obligated to maintain a non-Muslim wife. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the Hanafi school balances marital obligations with religious identity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of events
The ruling explicitly requires that apostasy occurs after the divorce (talāq). Pinpoint the order: first divorce, then apostasy.
If apostasy occurs before divorce, the marriage dissolves instantly, and no waiting-period maintenance is owed – a different case.
2
State the legal consequence
The text says 'her maintenance falls' (saqatat nafaqatuhā). This means she loses the right to maintenance from the moment of apostasy, even if the waiting period (iddah) is ongoing.
Maintenance does not gradually reduce; it ceases immediately.
3
Extract the rationale from the commentary
Commentators give two reasons: (1) apostasy is a form of nushuz (disobedience), which forfeits maintenance; (2) a Muslim cannot be obligated to maintain a non-Muslim (difference of religion blocks the obligation).
Both rationales are operative in the Hanafi school.
4
Consider the condition 'after divorce'
Why is it specified that apostasy occurs after divorce? Because if it occurred before, the marriage would end by apostasy itself, and the divorce would be irrelevant. The ruling highlights the precise timing.
This shows the school's precision in linking rulings to factual sequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۰) وان طلقها ثم ارتدت سقطت نفقتها
And if he divorces her, then she apostatizes, her maintenance falls.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the matn of the book on the topic of maintenance (nafaqah) during the waiting period. The ruling is that if a husband divorces his wife, and then she apostatizes (leaves Islam), her maintenance is nullified. The underlying reasoning, as explained in the commentary, is twofold: first, apostasy is a form of disobedience (nushuz) on the part of the wife, and second, a Muslim husband is not obliged to provide maintenance to a non-Muslim wife. This ruling is specific to the case where apostasy occurs after divorce.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance owed to wife during the waiting period after divorce
ارتدت (irtaddat): She apostatized (left Islam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a husband divorces his wife and then she apostatizes, what happens to her maintenance?
A) She keeps it until the end of the waiting period.
B) It falls immediately.
C) It is halved for the remaining period.
D) She must return all maintenance received.

Key Takeaway
A divorced wife's right to nafaqah is nullified the moment she apostatizes, due to nushuz and religious incompatibility.

Wife's Adultery with Step-son: Effect on Maintenance
Distinguishes maintenance effect based on timing relative to divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance when a wife commits adultery with her stepson, distinguishing the effect based on timing relative to divorce, and apply the principle to similar cases.

Core Idea
A wife's adultery before divorce cancels maintenance; after irrevocable divorce it does not.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a wife voluntarily gives access to her stepson. The ruling on her maintenance depends crucially on whether the act occurred before or after divorce. The legal principle is that maintenance is forfeited when the wife's misconduct causes the separation. We will unpack the proof and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
The act is the wife giving access to her stepson. The ruling splits based on whether this occurs before or after the divorce.
2
State the ruling for each timing
If after divorce, she has maintenance; if before, none.
3
Locate the dalil
The text cites a hadith from Fatimah bint Qays regarding the thrice-divorced woman.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith states that a thrice-divorced woman has no maintenance, implying that maintenance is only for revocable divorce. The commentators use this to support the principle that maintenance is due only when the separation is not caused by the wife's fault.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
Note that other schools may differ on the maintenance rules for a woman at fault.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱) وان مكنت ابن زوجها من نفسها فان كان بعد الطلاق فلها النفقة وان كان قبل الطلاق فلا نفقة لها. قال انما كان ذلك من سوء الخلق (ابوداؤد شريف رقم ۲۲۹۴). عن عامر عن فاطمة بنت قيس قالت قال رسول الله الله المطلقة ثلاثا لا سكنى لها ولا نفقة انما السكنى والنفقة لمن يملك الرجعة (دارقطني، كتاب الطلاق ج رابع ص ۱۵ رقم ۳۹۰۷).
And if she gives access to her husband's son to herself, then if it is after divorce, she has maintenance, and if it is before divorce, then no maintenance for her. He said: That was only from bad character (Abu Dawud no. 2294). From 'Amir from Fatimah bint Qays who said: The Messenger of Allah said: The thrice-divorced woman has no right to housing and no maintenance; housing and maintenance are only for the one who has the right of return (Darqutni, Book of Divorce, vol. 4, p. 15, no. 3907).
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents two related rulings. The first is the primary ruling: if the wife voluntarily gives access to her stepson (the husband's son from another wife) to herself for intercourse, the effect on her maintenance depends on the timing. If this occurs after an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in), then she still receives maintenance during her waiting period, because the divorce was already the cause of separation, not her act. If it occurs before the divorce, then her act of adultery causes the separation (since it makes marriage unlawful), so she loses her maintenance due to her disobedience. The passage then supports this principle with two narrations: one from Abu Dawud stating that such behavior is from bad character, and a hadith from Fatimah bint Qays indicating that a thrice-divorced woman has no maintenance, which the commentators use to argue that only a wife under revocable divorce is entitled to maintenance. The underlying principle is that maintenance is only given when the separation is not due to the wife's fault.

Key Terms
مكنت (makkānat): She gave access or enabled
ابن زوجها (ibn zawjihā): Her stepson (husband's son from another wife)
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance during the waiting period after divorce
طلقها (tallaqaha): He divorced her

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because the divorce already occurred
B) No, because she is disobedient
C) Only if she repents
D) It depends on the husband's wealth

Key Takeaway
Maintenance during iddah is forfeited only when the wife's misconduct is the cause of the separation, not when the separation has already been finalized.

When Maintenance Ceases: Imprisonment, Abduction, and Hajj without Mahram
Ruling that maintenance falls in three specific scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three cases where a wife loses her maintenance according to the Hanafi school and apply the underlying principle to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Maintenance ceases when the wife is unavailable due to her fault or irresistible force.

Maintenance (nafaqah) is generally obligatory on the husband for his wife, but it is conditional on the wife being available to the husband. This lesson examines three specific situations where the obligation falls: imprisonment for debt, abduction by force, and traveling for Hajj without a mahram. We will explore the proof from the companions and the legal reasoning behind these exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
Maintenance is wajib only when the wife is under the husband's control (ih'tibas) and obedient. If she becomes unavailable through her own fault or through coercion not attributable to the husband, the obligation drops.
The key condition is the possibility of retention (ih'tibas).
2
List the Three Exceptional Cases
From the text: (1) imprisonment for a debt, (2) abduction by force, (3) performing Hajj without a mahram. Identify the common element: in all three, the wife is not under her husband's control.
3
Examine the Proof (Dalil)
The text cites an athar from 'Amir: 'It is not upon a man to spend on his wife when the imprisonment is due to her.' This is a Qawl Sahabi, which is a proof in Hanafi usul. Understand that the phrase 'due to her' (min qibaliha) indicates fault.
The athar is recorded in Mussanaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Mussanaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Derive the Underlying Rationale
The 'illah (effective cause) is that the wife's absence prevents the husband from fulfilling his marital rights, and the cause is either her own action (debt, Hajj without mahram) or an external force (kidnapping) that is beyond the husband's control.
For kidnapping, note that the wife is a victim, but the obligation ceases because the retention is impossible.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Dispute
The Hanafi position is that maintenance falls in all three cases. However, other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may differ, especially in the case of kidnapping, arguing that the wife is not at fault. Understand that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is whether the husband must pay arrears if the wife returns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲) واذا حبست المرأة فى دين او غصبها رجل كرها فذهب بها او حجت مع غير محرم فلا نفقة لها. عن عامر قال ليس للرجل ان ينفق على امرأته اذا كان بالحبس من قبلها (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة 199 ص رابع ص 176 نمبر 19022 ر مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الرجل يغيب عن امرأته فلا يخفق عليها ج سابع ص 95 نمبر 13353)
And if the woman is imprisoned for a debt, or a man forcibly abducts her and takes her away, or she performs Hajj with a non-mahram, then no maintenance for her. From 'Amir: He said: It is not upon a man to spend on his wife when the imprisonment is due to her (Mussanaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...).
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage lists three scenarios where a wife's maintenance during the waiting period or generally is not obligatory. First, if she is imprisoned for a debt she owes, since her imprisonment results from her own failure to pay. Second, if she is kidnapped by force, her absence is not voluntary from her side, but the retention (ih'tibas) from her husband is not occurring, so maintenance falls. Third, if she goes for Hajj without a mahram, she has disobeyed Islamic law and is considered at fault. The athar from 'Amir supports the idea that if the imprisonment is due to the wife's own action, the husband is not obliged to spend on her. The underlying legal principle is that maintenance is contingent on the wife being available to the husband and the retention being possible due to the marriage contract. If the wife's absence or inability to be retained is caused by factors not attributable to the husband, the obligation ceases.

Key Terms
حبست (hubisat): She was imprisoned
غصبها (ghasabahā): He kidnapped/seized her by force
غير محرم (ghayr mahram): A person not within the prohibited degrees of marriage
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance (food, clothing, shelter) owed by husband to wife

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases does a wife lose her maintenance according to this passage?
A) She is imprisoned for a debt she owes
B) She is kidnapped by a stranger
C) She goes for Hajj without a mahram
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
A wife's maintenance ceases if she becomes unavailable due to her own fault or irresistible force, because the obligation is contingent on the possibility of retention.

Maintenance for Ill Wife in Husband's Home
Ruling statement on nafaqah during wife's illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on maintenance for a wife who falls ill in the husband's home and explain the underlying principle of ihtibas (retention).

Core Idea
Illness in the husband's home does not cancel the wife's right to maintenance.

This brief but precise ruling tackles a common concern: what happens to the wife's maintenance when she becomes ill? The Hanafi position is clear — as long as she remains in the marital home, her illness does not affect the husband's obligation. The reasoning, as explained in the commentaries, rests on the nature of maintenance as a right arising from the marriage contract itself, not from her ability to serve.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the wife falling ill while residing in the husband's house. The ruling is that she still receives maintenance (nafaqah).
The Arabic phrase 'فَلَها النَّفَقَةُ' clearly affirms the obligation.
2
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is ihtibas (retention) — the husband retains the wife in his household, and she is available to him. Illness does not prevent this retention; she remains in his custody.
Maintenance is not contingent on her being able to serve; it is a marital right.
3
Note the scope of the ruling
This applies as long as she stays in the husband's home. If she leaves without permission or goes to her parents' home, the ruling may differ.
The condition is her physical presence in the marital home.
4
Distinguish from related cases
Compare with a wife who falls ill before entering the husband's home (e.g., during the marriage but before cohabitation) — maintenance may be due once the home is ready. Also contrast with a wife who falls ill and is sent to a hospital with husband's consent — maintenance continues.
The key is whether she is 'in the husband's house' (fi bayt al-zawj).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳) واذا مرضت في منزل الزوج فلها النفقة
And if she falls ill in the husband's house, she has maintenance.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This short ruling establishes that if the wife becomes ill while residing in the husband's home, she is still entitled to maintenance. The reason, as explained in the commentary, is that her illness does not prevent her from being retained (ih'tibas) by the husband; she is still in his house and he may derive some benefit from her presence. The obligation of maintenance is not contingent on her being healthy or serving him; it is a right arising from the marriage contract itself. Therefore, even if she is bedridden, as long as she remains in the marital home and does not refuse him access, the husband must continue to provide for her.

Key Terms
مرضت (mariḍat): She fell ill
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance, financial support including food, clothing, and lodging
منزل الزوج (manzil al-zawj): The husband's house, the marital home
حيثما (haythumā): Wherever (not in text but implied by context)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wife falls ill and is bedridden in her husband's house. According to the ruling, does she still receive maintenance?
A) Yes, because she is in his house
B) No, because she cannot serve him
C) Only if she recovers
D) It depends on the husband's health

Key Takeaway
A wife's illness while in the husband's home does not cancel her right to maintenance; the obligation continues as long as she remains there.

The Obligation to Provide a Servant for the Wealthy Husband
Rules that a wealthy husband must provide one servant's maintenance but not more

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a husband's obligation to provide a servant for his wife and explain the proof from the hadith of Fatimah.

Core Idea
A wealthy husband must provide one servant; the obligation is limited to necessity.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling within the chapter of nafaqah (maintenance): the husband's duty to provide a servant for his wife if he is wealthy. The text establishes that the obligation is for one servant only, based on the example of Fatimah, the Prophet's daughter. We will explore the proof and the conditions attached.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is providing a servant for the wife. The ruling is wajib for a wealthy husband.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Fatimah complaining about grinding grain and seeking a servant.
The hadith is recorded in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's willingness to provide a servant shows the legitimacy of the need; the Hanafi school deduces obligation from this.
The proof is by implication (mafhum), thus zanni al-dalala.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may not require a servant at all, or may require more depending on custom.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position that one servant is sufficient is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٤) وتفرض على الزوج نفقة خادمها اذا كان موسرا ولا تُفرض لاكثر. عن على ان فاطمة عليها السلام شكت ما تلقى فى يدها من الرحى فاتت النبي لا تسأله خادما فلم تجده فذكرت ذلك لعائشة الخ (بخاري شريف، باب التكبير والتسبيح عند المنام ص ۹۳۵ نمبر ۶۳۱۸، كتاب الدعوات مسلم شريف، باب الدعاء عند النوم ص ۳۴۸ نمبر ۶۸۹۱/۲۷۱۳)
And the maintenance of her servant is imposed upon the husband when he is wealthy, and it is not imposed for more than one. From 'Ali that Fatimah, peace be upon her, complained about what she suffered from the hand-mill, so she came to the Prophet to ask for a servant, but she did not find him, so she mentioned that to 'Aishah, etc. (Bukhari... Muslim...).
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligation of a husband to provide maintenance for his wife's servant if he is wealthy (mūsir). The servant is to assist the wife in her household duties. However, only one servant is required; the obligation does not extend to more than one. The proof is taken from the incident of Fatimah, the daughter of the Prophet, who asked for a servant due to the hardship of manual labor. The Hanafi school interprets this as establishing that if the husband can afford it, he must provide a servant. The commentary also notes that Imam Abu Yusuf held that if the husband is very wealthy, two servants may be required (though that is not in the arabic text). The ruling is clear: one servant suffices, as that is the norm.

Key Terms
خادم (khādim): Servant
موسر (mūsir): Wealthy, one who can afford

Key Takeaway

When Nafaqah Ceases: Wife’s Imprisonment, Abduction, and Hajj without Mahram
Ruling with proof on cessation of nafaqah due to wife-caused detention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios in which a wife loses her right to nafaqah under Hanafi law and explain the underlying principle of availability (ihtibas).

Core Idea
Nafaqah is compensation for the wife’s availability – if she is unavailable due to her own cause, the obligation falls.

In Hanafi fiqh, the husband’s obligation to provide maintenance (nafaqah) is tied to the wife’s ability to be available for marital relations. This lesson explores three specific situations where the wife’s detention or absence originates from her side, leading to the cessation of nafaqah. We will examine the ruling, its rationale, and the supporting proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three cases mentioned in the text: imprisonment for debt, forced abduction, and performing Hajj without a mahram. Note that each involves the wife being unavailable due to a cause attributable to her.
The text treats these as instances where the detention (ihtibas) is 'from her side'.
2
Extract the common principle
The underlying principle is that nafaqah is compensation for tamkin (availability). When the wife's own action or situation makes her unavailable, the husband's obligation ceases. This principle is derived from the athar cited.
The key phrase is 'min qibaliha' (from her side).
3
Analyze the proof
The text cites an athar from 'Amir: 'The husband is not required to spend on his wife if the imprisonment is due to her own fault.' This is a transmission (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear: nafaqah is conditional on the wife not being the cause of her detention.
The athar is found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Hiba and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Consider a wife who travels for Umrah without a mahram. Since traveling without a mahram is her choice, the absence is from her side, and nafaqah is suspended by analogy to the Hajj case.
The 'illah (legal cause) is the wife causing her own unavailability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۱۳۹](۱۲) واذا حبست المرأة فى دين او غصبها رجل كرها فذهب بها او حجت مع غير محرم فلا نفقة لها إذا قید کر لی گئی عورت قرض میں یا اس کو کسی نے زبر دستی گصب کر لیا اور اس کو لے گیا یا محرم کے ساتھ حج کی تو اس کے لئے نفقہ نہیں ہے قرض کی وجہ سے عورت قید کر لی گئی تو عورت ہی کی غلطی کی وجہ سے احتباس ختم ہوا اس لئے اس کو قانونی طور پر نفقہ نہیں ملے گا۔ یوں شہر محبت میں دیدے تو بہتر ہے۔ اسی طرح کسی نے زبردستی کے طور پر عورت کو غصب کر لیا تو چونکہ اس کی جانب سے احتباس ختم ہو گیا اس لئے اس کو نفقہ نہیں ملے گا۔ اور محرم کے ساتھ حج کرنے چلی گئی اس صورت میں بھی عورت کی جانب سے احتباس ختم ہو گیا اس لئے اس کو نفقہ نہیں ملے گا۔ اثر گزر چکا ہے۔ عن عامر قال ليس للرجل ان ينفق على امرأته اذا كان بالحبس من قبلها (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی هیبت ۱۹۹ ص رابع ص ۱۷۶ نمبر ۱۹۰۲۲ ر مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب الرجل يغيب عن امرأته فلا يخفق علیها ج سابع ص ۹۵ نمبر ۱۳۳۵۳)
And if a woman is imprisoned for debt, or a man forcefully abducts her and takes her away, or she performs Hajj without a mahram, then there is no nafaqah for her. If a woman is imprisoned for debt, then because the detention occurred due to her own fault, she legally has no nafaqah. It is better if he gives her [something] in the city of love [?]. Similarly, if someone forcefully abducts a woman, since the detention is from her side, she will not receive nafaqah. And if she goes for Hajj with a non-mahram, here also the detention is from her side, so she will not receive nafaqah. The athar has passed: 'Amir said: The husband is not required to spend on his wife if the imprisonment is due to her own fault.'
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn with its commentary and proof. The ruling states that if a wife is separated from the husband due to reasons originating from her side—such as being imprisoned for her own debt, being abducted (even forcibly), or traveling for Hajj without a mahram—then the husband is not obligated to provide her maintenance (nafaqah). The underlying principle is that nafaqah is compensation for the wife's availability to the husband. When she is unavailable due to causes attributable to her, the obligation ceases. The commentator explains each scenario. The proof is an athar from 'Amir reported in the Musannaf of Ibn Abi Hiba and Abd al-Razzaq.

Key Terms
احتباس (ihtibas): Detention or confinement of the wife that prevents her from fulfilling marital duties

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) No, only if she is imprisoned for more than a year

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a wife's right to nafaqah is conditional on her being available to the husband through no fault of her own; if she is detained due to her own actions, the obligation ceases.

Nafaqah for a Wife Who Falls Ill at Home
Ruling on maintenance when wife becomes ill at home

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafaqah when a wife falls ill in the husband's home and explain why the principle of ihtibas does not apply.

Core Idea
Illness at home does not stop nafaqah; the wife's presence preserves benefit and ihtibas is absent.

This lesson addresses a practical question: if a wife becomes ill while living with her husband, is he still obligated to provide maintenance? The Hanafi school gives a clear ruling based on the concept of ihtibas (detention). By understanding this, you will see how the school balances the wife's rights with the husband's obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? A wife falling ill in the husband's home. The ruling: she is entitled to nafaqah (maintenance).
2
Recall the general condition for nafaqah
In Hanafi fiqh, a wife is entitled to nafaqah when she is available (tamkin) to the husband, allowing him to derive benefit from her.
3
Understand the exception: ihtibas
When the wife prevents the husband from any benefit (e.g., leaving the house without permission), ihtibas occurs and nafaqah is suspended.
Ihtibas must be from the wife's side and involve complete prevention of benefit.
4
Apply to the scenario
Illness at home does not prevent the husband from benefiting (e.g., companionship, household management). Therefore, ihtibas is not triggered and nafaqah continues.
Husband still benefits from her presence even if she cannot perform heavy chores.
5
State the ruling confidently
If she falls ill in his home, she receives nafaqah. This ruling is grounded in the non-occurrence of ihtibas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۱۴۰] (۱۳) واذا مرضت في منزل الزوج فلها النفقة إذا بیمار ہوگئی شوہر کے گھر میں تو اس کے لئے نفقہ ہوگا۔ چونکہ عورت شوہر کے گھر میں ہے اس لئے شوہر اس سے کچھ نہ کچھ فائدہ اٹھائے گا۔ اس لئے احتباس ختم نہیں ہوا اس لئے اس کو نفقہ ملے گا۔
And if she falls ill in the husband's house, she has the right to nafaqah. If she falls ill in the husband's house, then she will receive nafaqah. Since the woman is in the husband's house, the husband will derive some benefit from her. Therefore, the detention is not extinguished, so she will receive nafaqah.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling: if the wife becomes ill while residing in the husband's home, she continues to receive nafaqah. The reason given is that despite her illness, she is still physically present in the husband's house, and he can derive some benefit from her (such as companionship, managing the household, etc.). The key point is that her inability to fully serve due to illness does not amount to a complete loss of availability (ihtibas) from her side; rather, it is a natural contingency that does not break the marital obligation of maintenance.

Key Terms
احتباس (ihtibas): Detention or confinement that prevents the wife from being available to the husband, suspending nafaqah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife falls ill in the husband's home, according to the Hanafi school, the husband's obligation to provide nafaqah is:
A) Remains valid
B) Suspended until she recovers
C) Terminated
D) Reduced by half

Key Takeaway
A wife's illness at home does not extinguish her right to nafaqah because ihtibas has not occurred; she remains present and the husband can derive benefit.

Husband Must Provide One Servant if Wealthy
Ruling on obligation of providing a servant for the wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of servants a wealthy husband must provide for his wife and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding two servants for the extremely wealthy.

Core Idea
A wealthy husband must provide one servant; one suffices for all tasks.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of a wealthy husband to provide a servant for his wife. The matn states one servant is sufficient, but Imam Abu Yusuf argues two may be required for extreme wealth. We will explore the evidence and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that a wealthy husband must provide maintenance for one servant for his wife, and not more than one.
The ruling applies when the husband is musir (wealthy).
2
Understand the evidence
The hadith of Fatima requesting a servant from the Prophet indicates the husband's responsibility for service.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Examine the dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that if the husband is very wealthy, he must provide two servants: one for indoor and one for outdoor work.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is one servant, as per the matn and the majority.
Abu Yusuf's view is considered but not taken as the predominant fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And he must provide for the servant of his wife if he is wealthy, and not more than one. (14) It will be imposed on the husband the maintenance of a servant for his wife when he is wealthy, and not more than one. If the husband is wealthy enough to bear the maintenance of his wife's servant, then the maintenance of one servant for her service is obligatory on him. If the wife needs service and the husband has wealth, he should provide service for his wife, so the maintenance of a servant is obligatory on him. And since one servant suffices, doing both indoor and outdoor work, one servant is enough. (2) This is deduced from the hadith: From Ali that Fatima (as) complained of what she suffered from the hand-mill, so she came to the Prophet asking for a servant but did not find him, so she mentioned that to Aisha... (Bukhari, Muslim). In this hadith, Fatima asked for a servant, meaning that her maintenance is on her husband. Imam Abu Yusuf says that if the husband is very wealthy, the maintenance of two servants is obligatory: one for outdoor service and one for indoor service.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that a wealthy husband must provide the maintenance for one servant for his wife, and not more than one. The commentator explains that one servant is sufficient because it can perform both indoor and outdoor tasks. The proof is the hadith of Fatima (as) asking the Prophet for a servant, which indicates that the husband is responsible for providing service. However, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that if the husband is very wealthy, two servants are required—one for inside the house and one for outside. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school is the one servant, as per the text.

Key Terms
موسر (musir): Wealthy, capable of bearing the expense of a servant

Husband Must Provide Separate Accommodation
Ruling on husband's obligation to provide separate housing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the husband's obligation to provide separate housing and apply the exception of wife's consent.

Core Idea
A wife is entitled to her own separate dwelling, free from the husband's relatives.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: the husband must provide his wife with a separate home away from his relatives. This obligation is derived from the Quranic verse and the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). However, the wife may waive this right if she agrees to live with in-laws. Let us walk through the legal reasoning and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the core obligation: the husband must provide a separate dwelling (dar mufradah) for his wife.
This is a wajib (obligatory) duty in the Hanafi school.
2
Recognize the Condition
The dwelling must be separate, meaning no relatives of the husband reside in it. This condition safeguards the wife's privacy and security.
A separate room within the same house is not sufficient.
3
Note the Exception
If the wife willingly chooses to live with the husband's relatives, her consent overrides the default obligation.
The exception is based on the wife's choice, not the husband's.
4
Examine the Proof
The Quranic verse (65:1) uses the phrase 'biyutihinna' (their homes), implying a wife has a right to her own home. Also, the Prophet housed each wife separately.
The dalil provides strong basis for the ruling.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice, the husband must arrange an independent dwelling unless the wife agrees otherwise.
The ruling applies to all valid marriages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۱۴۲] (۱۵) وعليه ان يسكنها فى دار مفردة ليس فيها احد من اهله الا ان تختار ذلك ۱۴۳ [۲۱۴۲] (۱۵) شوہر پر لازم ہے کہ بیوی کو علیحدہ مکان میں رکھے جس میں شوہر کے رشتہ داروں میں سے کوئی نہ ہو، مگر یہ کہ عورت ان کے ساتھ رہنے پر راضی ہو۔ شوہر پر ایسا گھر لازم ہے جس میں شوہر کا کوئی رشتہ دار نہ رہتا ہو اور علیحدہ گھر ہو۔ البتہ عورت شوہر کے رشتہ دار کے ساتھ رہنے پر راضی ہو تو اس کی مرضی ہے۔ آیت میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ لا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن (الف) (آیت اسورۃ الطلاق ۶۵) بیوت کا مطلب ایسا گھر ہے جس میں آدمی رہ سکے۔ اس سے اشارہ ہوتا ہے کہ ایسے گھر میں رکھے جو علیحدہ ہوتا کہ عورت اپنا سامان وغیرہ حفاظت سے رکھ سکے (۲) حضور نے اپنے ازواج مطہرات کو علیحدہ علیحدہ کمروں میں رکھا تھا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ علیحدہ کمروں میں رکھے۔
And he must provide for her a separate house in which none of his family members reside, unless she chooses that [to live with them]. (15) It is obligatory on the husband to keep his wife in a separate house where none of his relatives live, unless the wife agrees to live with them. The husband must provide a house that does not have any of his relatives living in it, and it must be separate. However, if the wife agrees to live with the husband's relatives, it is her choice. There is an indication in the verse: 'Do not turn them out of their homes' (Surah al-Talaq 65). The word 'homes' means a house in which one can live. This indicates that he should place her in a separate house so that she can keep her belongings safely. Also, the Prophet kept his pure wives in separate rooms, which shows that he should provide separate rooms.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that the husband must provide his wife with a separate house not shared with his relatives, unless the wife willingly agrees to live with them. The commentator explains the reasoning: the wife needs privacy and security for her belongings. The proof is from the Quranic verse 'Do not turn them out of their homes' (65:1), which implies that the wife is entitled to her own dwelling. Additionally, the practice of the Prophet who housed each of his wives in separate rooms serves as a model. The wife's consent to live with in-laws is acceptable as it is her choice.

Key Terms
دار مفردة (dar mufradah): A separate house or dwelling that the wife occupies alone without the husband's relatives

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He can force her to live with his mother
B) He must provide a separate house where no relative lives
C) He may provide a separate room in the same house
D) The wife must obey and live with the mother

Key Takeaway
The husband must provide a separate dwelling for his wife, free from his relatives, unless she consents to live with them.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
beginner
6 min
No Separation Due to Husband's Inability to Pay Nafaqah
Ruling that poverty does not invalidate marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband cannot pay nafaqah and explain the wife's recourse.

Core Idea
Poverty does not break the marriage — the wife borrows on his credit.

This lesson addresses a common concern: what happens if a husband cannot afford to maintain his wife? In the Hanafi school, the marriage remains intact. The wife is advised to borrow for her needs, creating a debt on the husband. This ruling emphasizes the permanence of marriage over financial hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on the husband's inability to provide nafaqah. The ruling is that separation (tafriq) is not made.
2
Understand the consequence: no separation
The marriage contract remains valid. The wife does not have the right to annulment due to poverty.
3
Recognize the wife's option: borrowing
The wife is told 'istadayini' (borrow on his account). This loan becomes a debt on the husband.
4
Note the underlying rationale
Poverty is considered a temporary condition. The marital bond is too strong to be broken by financial incapacity alone.
5
Compare with other schools
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow faskh (annulment) in such cases. The Hanafi position differs based on istihsan and the principle that nafaqah is a debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۱۴۵] (۱۸) و من اعسر بنفقة امرأته لم يفرق بينهما ويقال لها استديني [۲۱۴۵] (۱۸) کوئی شخص عاجز ہو جائے بیوی کے نفقے سے تو دونوں میں تفریق نہیں کی جائے اور بیوی سے کہا جائے گا کہ تو اس کے ذمہ قرض لیتی رھ کوئی آدمی بیوی کو نفقہ دینے سے عاجز ہو جائے تو دونوں کے درمیان تفریق نہیں کی جائے گی بلکہ عورت کو کہا جائے گا کہ شوہر کے ذمے قرض لیتی رہے۔
And whoever is unable to pay the nafaqah of his wife, separation is not made between them, and she is told: 'Borrow on his account.' (18) If a person becomes unable to provide his wife's nafaqah, then separation is not made between them. Instead, the woman is told: 'Continue borrowing on the husband's responsibility.'
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This is a final ruling on the husband's inability to pay maintenance. Unlike some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i), the Hanafi school does not allow annulment of marriage due to the husband's poverty. The marriage remains intact, and the wife is advised to borrow money for her expenses, which becomes a debt on the husband. The reasoning is that poverty is a temporary condition that can change, and the marital bond is not broken by financial incapacity alone. The wife has the right to demand repayment later when the husband becomes able.

Key Terms
أعسر (a'sar): To become unable to pay, insolvent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the wife instructed to do if her husband cannot pay nafaqah?
A) Seek divorce from a judge
B) Borrow on his account
C) Leave the marital home
D) File a complaint with the authorities

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a husband's financial hardship does not dissolve the marriage; the wife's right to maintenance remains as a debt.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
beginner
6 min
Husband must house wife separately unless she consents otherwise
Ruling on husband's obligation to provide separate accommodation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the husband's duty to provide separate housing and apply the exception of the wife's voluntary consent.

Core Idea
Husband must provide separate housing; wife's consent is the sole exception to sharing with in-laws.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental ruling within the Hanafi school on marital maintenance: the husband's duty to provide a separate dwelling for his wife, free from his relatives. This obligation is rooted in the Qur'anic command to honor the wife's right to a private home. We will explore the proof from the Qur'an, the precise scope of the obligation, and the key exception when the wife willingly agrees to live with relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific obligation? The husband must provide housing (sukna) for his wife. What is the hukm? It is wajib (obligatory), part of nafaqah.
Note that it is wajib, not fard, due to the nature of the proof.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The Qur'anic verse 'la tukhrijuhunna min buyutihinna' (Do not turn them out of their houses) from Surah al-Talaq 65:1. Also the Sunnah of the Prophet housing each wife separately.
The verse implies a proper, private dwelling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the verse prove the ruling? The phrase 'min buyutihinna' (from their houses) indicates that the wives have houses that belong to them, implying the husband must provide such a house. The imperative context (do not turn out) reinforces that housing is a right.
The dalala is zanni because the verse is primarily about iddah, but by qiyas it applies to marriage.
4
Identify the exception
What is the exception? 'Illa an takhtara dhalika' (unless she chooses that). The wife may voluntarily consent to live with the husband's relatives, but she cannot be forced.
Consent must be free and informed; coercion invalidates the exception.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
What is the relied-upon position? The obligation stands as stated; the exception is only with the wife's choice. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and there is no major intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
This ruling is muttafaq alayh among the schools; differences are minor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعليه ان يسكنها فى دار مفردة ليس فيها احد من اهله الا ان تختار ذلك
And it is upon him to house her in a separate dwelling in which none of his relatives are present, unless she chooses that.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This is a ruling on the husband's obligation to provide maintenance (nafaqah) for his wife, specifically the housing component. The passage states that the husband must provide a dwelling that is separate and private for his wife, meaning the house should not be shared with any of the husband's relatives (such as his mother, siblings, or children from another marriage). The only exception is if the wife herself willingly chooses to live with them. This obligation is derived from the Qur'anic verse: 'Do not turn them out of their houses' (Surah al-Talaq, 65:1), which implies a proper dwelling. The Sunnah is also cited: the Prophet (peace be upon him) housed each of his wives in separate rooms. The Urdu commentary adds that the house must be such that the wife can securely keep her belongings. This ruling emphasizes the wife's right to privacy and comfort.

Key Terms
دار مفردة (dar mufradah): A separate dwelling where no relatives of the husband reside, ensuring the wife's privacy and comfort.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition may a husband house his wife with his relatives?
A) When the husband's financial situation is difficult
B) When the wife willingly chooses to live with them
C) When the relatives are women only
D) When the wife has no children

Key Takeaway
A wife has a right to separate housing; only her voluntary consent allows an exception.

beginner

Husband's Right to Control Entry but Not Communication
Ruling on husband's right to control access to the marital home

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the husband's right to prevent entry into his home and distinguish between permissible prevention of entry and impermissible prevention of looking and speaking.

Core Idea
Husband may forbid entry but not forbid looking or speaking to his wife.

A common area of marital tension is the husband's authority over the home and the wife's relationship with her family. This passage clarifies the Hanafi balance: the husband owns the home and can decide who enters, but he may not use that authority to cut off all contact. Understanding this distinction prevents both overreach and misunderstanding of Islamic marital rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two-part ruling
First, the husband may prevent her parents, her child from another husband, and other relatives from entering the house. Second, he does not prevent them from looking at her or speaking with her at any time.
The ruling is clear in granting authority over entry but explicitly preserving communication.
2
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The right to prevent entry is based on the husband's ownership of the home. Ownership gives him the authority to exclude others. However, preventing looking or speaking would sever family ties (qat' rahmi), which is forbidden in Shariah. Thus, the second part is based on preventing harm and preserving obligations.
The proof is rational: property rights vs. prohibition of cutting family ties.
3
Recognize the balance (hanafi tarjih)
The Hanafi school strikes a balance: the husband's property right is respected, but it does not extend to isolating the wife from her family. The wife's right to maintain family relations is protected.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from more extreme interpretations.
4
Apply to real scenarios
Consider: can the husband prevent his wife's mother from entering? Yes, if he owns the home. Can he forbid phone calls? No, because that prevents communication. The ruling applies to physical entry, not other forms of contact.
Electronic communication is analogous to speaking; preventing it would also be impermissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللزوج ان يمنع والديها وولدها من غيره واهلها من الدخول عليها ( ۱۴ ) ولا يمنعهم من النظر اليها ولا من كلامهم معها في اى وقت اختاروا
And the husband has the right to prevent her parents, and her child from another [husband], and her relatives from entering upon her. And he does not prevent them from looking at her nor from speaking with her at any time they choose.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage addresses the husband's authority over the marital home. Since the house belongs to the husband, he can decide who enters. He may lawfully forbid the wife's parents, her children from a previous marriage, and other relatives from entering the house. However, this right does not extend to preventing them from simply seeing her or speaking with her when they meet outside or through a window or door, as long as they do not enter. The Urdu commentary explains that preventing speech would constitute cutting family ties (qat' rahmi), which is forbidden in Shariah. This ruling balances the husband's property rights with the wife's right to maintain family relations.

Key Terms
ولدها من غيره (waladuha min ghayrihi): The wife's child from a previous or other husband, not the current husband's child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What can a husband prevent regarding his wife's relatives?
A) They cannot speak with her at all
B) They cannot enter his house
C) They cannot look at her
D) They cannot visit her in her parents' home

Key Takeaway
The husband's right to control access to his home does not extend to preventing his wife from maintaining family ties through looking or speaking.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
6 min
No separation if husband cannot afford maintenance; wife may take debt
Ruling on husband's inability to pay nafaqah and the inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a husband's inability to pay nafaqah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, insolvency does not dissolve marriage; the wife's remedy is a loan, not separation.

When a husband cannot afford his wife's maintenance, a critical question arises: does the marriage end? The Hanafi school says no, while the Shafi'i school says yes. This lesson examines the proofs behind each position and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its remedy
Identify the ruling: no separation, wife takes a loan on the husband's credit. Note that the marriage remains valid.
2
Identify the Hanafi dalil
Locate the proof: hadith of Hind bint Utba (Bukhari) where the Prophet allowed her to take from Abu Sufyan's wealth. Also athar from Hasan al-Basri and Zuhri.
The hadith implies the marriage continues while the husband owes the debt.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that separation is required. His proof is the statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab who claimed it is from the Sunnah.
The Shafi'i school considers maintenance a condition for the marriage to continue.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
Hanafis argue that the hadith of Hind is stronger and more direct. Sa'id's claim is not universally accepted as Sunnah; other Sahaba (Umar, Ali) held the Hanafi view.
Rejection of Sa'id's statement as mutawatir; preference for the general principle that marriage is not dissolved by poverty.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, marriage remains, wife can borrow. Under Shafi'i, wife can seek annulment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اعسر بنفقة امرأته لم يفرق بينهما ويقال لها استديني عليه ... امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ تفریق کر دی جائے گی۔ سألت سعيد ابن المسيب عن الرجل يعجز عن نفقة امرأته فقال يفرق بينهما فقلت سنة ؟ فقال سنة
And whoever is unable [to pay] the maintenance of his wife, separation is not made between them, and it is said to her: 'Take a loan against him.' ... Imam Shafi'i says that separation will be made. I asked Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab about a man unable to pay his wife's maintenance; he said: 'Separation is made between them.' I said: 'Is it from the Sunnah?' He said: 'Yes, from the Sunnah.'
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on a husband who cannot afford his wife's maintenance. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Hanafi school, the couple should not be separated (i.e., the marriage is not dissolved). Instead, the wife is instructed to take a loan on the husband's credit to cover her expenses. The reason is that separation would cause greater harm than the loss of maintenance, and the loan compensates for the loss. The ruling is supported by the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the incident of Hind bint Utba, who took from Abu Sufyan's wealth without his knowledge. Also, athar (reports) from Hasan al-Basri and Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri confirm the Hanafi view. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the marriage should be annulled (dissolved) because maintenance is an essential marital right, and its permanent lack causes hardship. He relies on the statement of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab who claimed it is a Sunnah. The Urdu commentary adds that in contemporary times, because it is difficult for a woman to take a loan, a judge may order separation if circumstances are dire, but the original Hanafi position remains as stated.

Key Terms
إعسار (i'sar): Inability to pay maintenance due to poverty or lack of means.
استديني (istadini): She is told to take a loan (on the husband's credit) to cover her nafaqah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling when a husband becomes permanently unable to pay nafaqah?
A) The marriage is annulled immediately
B) The wife must be patient without any recourse
C) The wife may take a loan on the husband's credit
D) The husband is jailed until he pays

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a husband's inability to pay maintenance does not dissolve the marriage; the wife may take a loan on his credit.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate

Maintenance from Absent Husband's Property upon Acknowledgment
Ruling on maintenance from absent husband's acknowledged property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on assigning maintenance from an absent husband's property based on third-party acknowledgment and identify the three categories of dependents entitled to maintenance.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment of both property and marriage by a third party suffices for the judge to assign maintenance from the property.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario in family law: when a husband is absent but his property is held by someone who acknowledges both the property and the marriage. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance on how to ensure the dependents are not left without support. The ruling demonstrates the school's concern for preventing hardship in cases of absence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage and identify the key elements: an absent husband, property held by a third party, and acknowledgment by that third party of both the property and the marriage.
The scenario excludes cases where the holder denies either the property or the marriage.
2
Recognize the role of acknowledgment
Understand that the third party's acknowledgment (iqrar) serves as sufficient proof. In Hanafi law, a credible acknowledgment is binding and eliminates the need for further evidence of the marriage.
The acknowledgment must be explicit and cover both the property's ownership and the marital relationship.
3
List the dependents covered
Identify the three categories of dependents for whom the judge can assign maintenance: the wife, the husband's young children (from the absent husband), and the husband's parents.
Young children are those who have not reached the age of independence; parents include both mother and father.
4
Understand the judge's duty
The judge (qadi) is obligated (wajib) to assign maintenance from the acknowledged property. This is a means of fulfilling the husband's duty of nafaqah despite his absence.
The ruling applies to both movable and immovable property held by the third party.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا غاب الرجل وله مال فى يد رجل يعترف به وبالزوجية فرض قاضی غائب کی بیوی کا نفقہ اور اس کے چھوٹے بچوں کا نفقہ اور اس کے والدین کا نفقہ
And if a man is absent and he has property in the hand of a man who acknowledges it and acknowledges the marriage, the judge assigns: for the absent [husband]'s wife her maintenance, and for his young children their maintenance, and for his parents their maintenance.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This ruling deals with the scenario where a husband is absent (e.g., traveling or missing) but has property held by a third party. If that third party acknowledges both that he holds the property for the absent husband and that the woman claiming to be his wife is indeed his wife, then the judge can order that maintenance be paid from that property to the wife, the husband's young children, and his parents. The Urdu commentary notes that once the acknowledgment is made, no further proof of the marriage is needed. This ruling ensures that the dependents of an absent person are not deprived of their maintenance when there is accessible property and an acknowledgment of the relationship.

Key Terms
يعترف به وبالزوجية (ya'tarifu bihi wa bil-zawjiyyah): Acknowledges both the property (that it belongs to the absent husband) and the marriage (that the woman is his wife).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Whose maintenance may the judge assign from the absent husband's property upon acknowledgment?
A) Only the wife
B) The wife and her children (including those from previous marriage)
C) The wife, young children of the husband, and his parents
D) All relatives of the husband

Key Takeaway
Acknowledgment by the holder of the absent husband's property of both the property and marriage is sufficient for the judge to order maintenance for the wife, young children, and parents.
