Mother Not Obliged to Breastfeed; Father Must Provide Wet Nurse
Ruling with proof on breastfeeding obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a mother is not obliged to breastfeed and identify the Quranic evidence (2:233) for this position.

Core Idea
Breastfeeding is a mother's right, not a duty; the father must provide for the child's nursing.

Who is legally responsible for feeding an infant? In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation rests squarely on the father. This lesson examines whether the mother can be compelled to breastfeed and what happens if she refuses. We will unpack the ruling and its proof from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is breastfeeding an infant. The ruling is that it is not obligatory (wajib) on the mother. It is recommended (mandub) if she is able. The father is obligated to provide for the child, which includes hiring a wet nurse if needed.
Note the two-part ruling: mother's non-obligation, father's obligation to hire.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is Quran 2:233. Three parts of the verse are cited: (a) the father's duty to provide maintenance, (b) prohibition of harming the mother through breastfeeding, (c) permission to hire a substitute wet nurse.
All three parts support the overall ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
From part (a), the father's obligation to provide includes providing a wet nurse. Part (b) implies that if breastfeeding harmed the mother, she cannot be forced. Part (c) explicitly permits hiring, which would be unnecessary if the mother were obliged.
The combination of these three implies the mother's choice.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that the mother is obliged to breastfeed if she is the wife and the child is hers, unless there is a valid excuse. Hanafi gives her the free choice.
The difference stems from a different reading of the same verse.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that the mother cannot be compelled. This is the view of Zahir al-Riwayah and is the operative ruling for fatwa.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كان الصغير رضيعا فليس على امه ان ترضعه ويستأجر له الاب من ترضعه عندها [۲۱۵۶] (۲۹) اگر بچہ دودھ پینے والا ہو تو ماں پر لازم نہیں ہے کہ اس کو دودھ پلائے اور باپ اس کے لئے اجرت پر رکھے ایسی عورت کو جو ماں کے پاس دودھ پلائے۔ کوئی مجبوری ہو تو ماں پر بچے کو دودھ پلانا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اگر مجبوری نہ ہو تو اس کو دودھ پلانا چاہئے کیونکہ اس کا بچہ ہے۔ اگر نہ پلائے تو باپ ایسی عورت کو اجرت پر لے جو ماں کے پاس رہ کر دودھ پلائے۔ او پر آیت گزری کہ باپ پر بچے کا نفقہ لازم ہے۔ وعلی المولود له رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف (الف) (آیت ۲۳۳ سورة البقرة ٢) اور ماں پر دودھ پلانا لازم نہیں ہے اس کے لئے اس آیت میں اشارہ ہے۔ لا تضار والدة بولدها ولا مولود له بولده (ب) آیت ۲۳۳ سورة البقرة (۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ والدہ کو دودھ پلانے میں نقصان نہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ اور دوسری عورت کو دودھ پلانے کے لئے اجرت پر لے اس کے لئے یہ آیت ہے۔ وان اردتم ان تستر ضعوا اولادكم فلا جناح عليكم اذا سلمتم ما آتیتم بالمعروف (ج ) ( آیت ۲۳۳ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے پتہ چلا کہ دودھ پلانے کے لئے کسی عورت کو اجرت پر لے۔ اور چونکہ پرورش کا حق ماں کو ہے اس لئے ماں کے پاس رہ کر دودھ پلائے ۔
If the child is a suckling, then it is not upon his mother to breastfeed him, and the father hires for him a woman who will breastfeed him at her (the mother's) place. [2156] (29) If the child is a suckling, it is not obligatory on the mother to breastfeed him, and the father hires for him a woman who will breastfeed him at the mother's place. If there is a compulsion, then it is not necessary for the mother to breastfeed the child. If there is no compulsion, she should breastfeed him because he is her child. If she does not breastfeed, then the father hires a woman who will breastfeed him while living at the mother's place. The verse that passed indicates that the maintenance of the child is obligatory on the father: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is reasonable' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:233). And that breastfeeding is not obligatory on the mother is indicated in this verse: 'No mother shall be harmed through her child, nor father through his child' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:233). From this verse it is understood that the mother should not be harmed by breastfeeding. And for hiring another woman to breastfeed, this verse is: 'And if you wish to have your children nursed by a substitute, there is no blame upon you as long as you pay what you give according to what is reasonable' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:233). This verse shows that a woman can be hired to breastfeed. And since the right of custody belongs to the mother, she should breastfeed at her place.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This ruling addresses the situation when a child is an infant needing breastfeeding. The mother is under no legal compulsion to breastfeed; she may choose to do so voluntarily. If she refuses, the father must hire a wet nurse, and the nurse must perform the breastfeeding at the mother's home—because the mother has the right of custody (hadanah) and the child should not be separated from her. The proof is drawn from three parts of Quran 2:233: (a) the father's duty to provide, (b) the prohibition of harming the mother through breastfeeding, and (c) the permission to hire a substitute nurse. The commentary notes that if there is no exigency, it is recommended for the mother to breastfeed, but it is not legally obligatory (wajib).

Key Terms
رضاع (rida'): Breastfeeding of an infant; the act of suckling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the father required to do if the mother refuses to breastfeed?
A) Force the mother to breastfeed
B) Hire a wet nurse to breastfeed at the mother's home
C) Take the child away from the mother
D) Provide formula only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, breastfeeding is a mother's choice, not an obligation; the father bears the duty to ensure the child is fed, whether by the mother (voluntarily) or by a hired wet nurse.

Prohibition of Hiring Wife or Woman in Iddah to Breastfeed
Ruling disallowing hiring one's wife or a woman in iddah to nurse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring one's wife or a woman in iddah for breastfeeding and explain the Quranic proof and the underlying rationale.

Core Idea
Hiring one's wife or a woman in iddah to nurse is impermissible because it contradicts the mother's inherent duty.

This lesson addresses a specific family law scenario: a father hiring his own wife or the mother of his child (who is in iddah) to breastfeed their child. The text clearly prohibits it based on the Quranic directive that mothers should nurse their children, implying a natural responsibility, and on the fact that the wife is already entitled to maintenance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is hiring one's wife or a woman in iddah to breastfeed. The ruling is 'not permissible' (la yajuz), which in Hanafi fiqh is typically understood as haram.
Note that the ruling applies specifically to the wife or a woman in iddah from the same husband.
2
Understand the rationale
The mother is already obligated to care for the child; if she is not forced, she should breastfeed voluntarily. Hiring her implies she is not compelled, so it is not allowed.
The commentary states that if there is no compulsion, the mother should breastfeed without pay.
3
Examine the dalil
The Quranic verse (2:233) instructs mothers to breastfeed their children for two complete years. This establishes a duty, not a paid service.
The dalal is zanni because the imperative form may indicate recommendation or obligation; Hanafi interprets it as a duty.
4
Note the Hanafi position and cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school holds it is not permissible (mufta bihi). Some other schools may allow hiring if the mother demands payment, but Hanafi rejects this due to the inherent duty.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان استأجرها وهي زوجته او معتدته لترضع ولدها لم يجز [۲۱۵۷] (۳۰) اگر اجرت پر لیا بیوی کو یا اپنی عدت گزارنے والی کو تا کہ اس کے بچے کو دودھ پلائے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ ا شوہر نے اپنی بیوی یا طلاق کی عدت گزارنے والی کو اجرت پر لیا تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہ بچے کی ماں ہے اس لئے اگر مجبوری نہ ہو تو اس کو ہی دودھ پلانا چاہئے ۔ اور جب اجرت لیکر دودھ پلانے پر تیار ہوئی تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس کو دودھ پلانے کی مجبوری نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو اجرت پر لینا جائز نہیں ہے (۲) آیت میں ہے کہ والدہ کو دودھ پلانا چاہئے۔ والوالدات يرضعن اولادهن حولين كاملين لمن اراد ان يتم الرضاعة ( و ) ( آیت ۲۳۳ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ والدہ دودھ پلائے اس لئے اپنی والدہ کو اجرت پر لینا ٹھیک نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ نفقہ وغیرہ لے رہی ہے۔
If he hires her while she is his wife or his woman in iddah to breastfeed his child, it is not permissible. [2157] (30) If he hires his wife or a woman in iddah from a divorce so that she breastfeeds his child, it is not permissible. The husband hired his wife or the woman in iddah from divorce; it is not permissible. She is the mother of the child, so if there is no compulsion, she should breastfeed him. And when she is ready to breastfeed for wage, it means she is not compelled to breastfeed. Therefore, hiring her is not permissible. (2) The verse says that the mothers should breastfeed: 'And mothers shall breastfeed their children for two whole years, for those who wish to complete the breastfeeding' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:233). From this verse it is understood that the mother should breastfeed, so hiring the mother is not correct because she is already receiving maintenance and other support.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This ruling states that a father cannot enter into a paid contract with his own wife or a woman in iddah from him to breastfeed his child. The reason is twofold: first, the mother is already obligated to care for the child, and if she is not forced, she should breastfeed voluntarily; second, the Quranic verse (2:233) instructs mothers to breastfeed their children, implying a duty, not a paid service. Since the wife is already entitled to maintenance from the husband, hiring her would be double compensation. The commentary clarifies that if there is no compulsion (like illness), the mother should breastfeed without pay. If she demands payment, it indicates she is not obligated, so hiring her is impermissible.

Key Terms
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman in her iddah (waiting period) after divorce or death of husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because she is not skilled
B) Because she is already obligated to breastfeed and receives maintenance
C) Because the child will not accept it
D) Because it is too expensive

Key Takeaway
The Quranic instruction to mothers to breastfeed establishes a duty, not a paid service, so hiring one's wife or woman in iddah is invalid.

Hiring a Divorced Woman After Iddah for Breastfeeding
Ruling allowing hiring of divorced woman after iddah to nurse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a divorced woman to breastfeed after her iddah and identify the condition that makes it permissible.

Core Idea
After iddah, a divorced woman is a stranger; hiring her for breastfeeding is like hiring any wet nurse—permissible.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a father cannot hire his wife or a woman in iddah to breastfeed his child because she is entitled to maintenance and still tied to the marriage. But what if the iddah has ended? This lesson clarifies that once the iddah expires, the woman becomes a stranger (ajnabiyyah) and the prohibition lifts, making the hiring permissible just as with any other wet nurse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiring a divorced woman to breastfeed the father's child. The ruling is permissible (ja'iz).
The permissibility is conditional on the expiry of iddah.
2
Identify the condition that changes the ruling
The key condition is that the woman's iddah must have expired. If she is still in iddah or still a wife, it is not permissible.
The text explicitly states 'if her iddah has expired'.
3
Understand the reason (sabab) for the change
After iddah, the woman is no longer entitled to maintenance from the father and is no longer a wife; she is now a stranger (ajnabiyyah). Hence, hiring her is like hiring any other wet nurse.
The commentary expands that the prohibition only applied while she was still in the marital bond.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان انقضت عدتها فاستأجرها على ارضاعه جاز [۲۱۵۸] (۳۱) اور اگر اس کی عدت ختم ہو گئی اور اس کو اجرت پر لیا دودھ پلانے کے لئے تو جائز ہے۔ بیوی عدت گزار رہی تھی اس دوران عدت ختم ہو گئی۔ اب اس کو اپنے بچے کے دودھ پلانے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا تو جائز ہے۔ اب یہ بیوی نہیں رہی اور نہ شوہر سے نفقہ لے رہی ہے بلکہ اجنبیہ بن گئی اس لئے اس کو اجرت پر لینا جائز ہے۔
And if her iddah has expired, and he hires her for his child's breastfeeding, it is permissible. [2158] (31) And if her iddah has ended and he hires her to breastfeed, it is permissible. The wife was in iddah; during that time the iddah ended. Now hiring her to breastfeed her child is permissible. Now she is no longer a wife and is not receiving maintenance from the husband, but has become a stranger (ajnabiyyah), so hiring her is permissible.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This ruling clarifies the exception to the previous prohibition. If a woman was in iddah and that period expires, she becomes a stranger (ajnabiyyah) to the father. Therefore, hiring her to breastfeed the child is now permissible, just as hiring any other wet nurse would be. The prohibition only applied while she was still his wife or in his iddah, because she was entitled to maintenance and had a certain duty.

Key Terms
اجنبية (ajnabiyyah): A woman who is a stranger, i.e., not a mahram or wife.

Key Takeaway
After a woman's iddah expires, hiring her to breastfeed is permissible as she becomes a stranger (ajnabiyyah), removing the earlier prohibition.

Mother's Priority to Breastfeed When Wage is Matched
Ruling on mother's right to breastfeed for same wage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which the mother has priority to breastfeed over a hired stranger and explain the consequence of demanding a higher wage.

Core Idea
The mother's right to breastfeed is conditional on matching the wage of a hired nurse.

This lesson addresses a common family situation: when the father refuses to hire the mother as a wet nurse and brings another woman, the mother still has a right to breastfeed if she agrees to the same wage. This ruling balances the mother's custody interest with the father's financial obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key parties and actions
The father refuses to hire the mother and brings a stranger (ajnabiyyah). The mother then offers to breastfeed for the same wage as the stranger.
2
State the condition for mother's priority
The mother must agree to the exact same wage (mithl ujrat al-ajnabiyyah) as the stranger.
She may not demand more.
3
Determine the legal effect
If the condition is met, the mother is more entitled (ahaqq) to breastfeed the child. This is a right of priority based on her being the mother and the child's welfare.
4
Identify the exception
If the mother demands a higher wage, the father is not compelled to hire her; he may hire the stranger instead.
The mother loses her priority if she asks for more.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قال الاب لا استأجرها وجاء بغيرها فرضيت الام بمثل اجرة الاجنبية كانت الام احق به وان سکتی ہو تو باپ ایسی عورت کو اجرت پر لے جو ماں کے پاس رہ کر دودھ پلائے۔ [۲۱۵۹] (۳۲) اور اگر باپ نے کہا نہیں اجرت پر لوں گا والدہ کو اور کسی دوسری عورت کو لے آئے، پس ماں راضی ہوگئی اجنبیہ کی اجرت مثل پر تو ماں اس کی زیادہ حقدار ہوگی۔ اور اگر وہ اجرت زیادہ طلب کرے تو شوہر کو اس پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
And if the father says, 'I will not hire her' and brings another woman, and the mother agrees to the same wage as the stranger, then the mother is more entitled to him. And if she is silent, then the father hires a woman who will breastfeed him while staying at the mother's place. [2159] (32) And if the father says, 'I will not hire the mother' and brings another woman, and the mother agrees to the wage equal to that of the stranger, then the mother has more right to him. And if she demands a higher wage, the husband will not be forced to accept it.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This ruling provides the procedure when the father refuses to hire the mother and brings another wet nurse. If the mother is willing to breastfeed for the same wage as the stranger, she has the superior right (ahaqq) to breastfeed the child. This is because the mother's custody right and the child's welfare favor the mother. However, if she demands more than the stranger's wage, the father is not compelled to hire her; he may hire the stranger instead. The commentary emphasizes that the mother's right is conditional on matching the wage.

Key Terms
احق (ahaqq): More entitled or having superior right; here, the mother is more entitled to breastfeed than a stranger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does the mother have priority to breastfeed over a hired stranger?
A) She is always prioritized.
B) If she agrees to the same wage as the stranger.
C) If she demands less wage.
D) If she is the father's relative.

Key Takeaway
The mother's priority to breastfeed is conditional on matching the hired nurse's wage; if she demands more, the father may choose the nurse.

Hiring Wife or Divorcée to Nurse Her Own Child Invalid
Ruling with proofs on hiring wife or 'iddah woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring one's wife or a woman in 'iddah to nurse the child and explain the Quranic evidence for the prohibition.

Core Idea
A mother is already obliged to nurse; hiring her for what she must do is a defective contract (fasid).

You might think a father can hire anyone to nurse his child, including the child's own mother. But Hanafi law draws a critical distinction: if the mother is still in the marriage or observing 'iddah, hiring her is invalid because she is already obligated to nurse without wage. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its Quranic basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Read the passage: the act is hiring (isti'jar) one's wife or a woman in 'iddah (mu'taddah) to nurse the child. The ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuz).
Note the exception: after 'iddah ends, hiring is permissible.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
Why is it invalid? Because the mother is already obliged to nurse the child if she is healthy and not harmed. Hiring her for what she must already do turns a duty into a paid service, which is fasid (defective).
This is based on the mother's inherent obligation, not on a mutual contract.
3
Locate the Quranic evidence
The author cites Quran 2:233: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing... No mother should be harmed through her child... And if you wish to have your children nursed by a substitute, there is no blame upon you.'
Three proofs from the same verse: (a) father provides for the mother, (b) no harm to mother, (c) permissibility to hire others implies hiring the mother is not the default.
4
Trace the derivation (wajh al-dalalah)
From the command 'mothers shall nurse their children' and the phrase 'no harm', the Hanafis deduce that the mother's nursing is a duty, not a service for hire. The permissibility to hire others shows that hiring the mother would be an exception, and since no exception is made, it remains invalid.
The evidence is qat'i in transmission but zanni in meaning – it is interpreted.
5
Note the scope and exception
The ruling only applies as long as the mother is in the marriage or 'iddah. After her 'iddah expires, the obligation lifts, and hiring her becomes valid. Also, if the mother demands more than a stranger's wage, the father is not forced to pay it.
This shows the ruling is tied to the mother's ongoing marital status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۱۵۷ (۳۰) فان استأجرها وهي زوجته او مـعتـدتـه لترضع ولدها لم يجز ۱۵۸) (۳۱) وان انقضت عدتها فاستأجرها على ارضاعه جاز [۲۱۵۹ (۳۲) وان قال الاب لا استأجرها وجاء بغيرها فرضيت الام بمثل اجرة الاجنبية كانت الام احق به وان سکتی ہو تو باپ ایسی عورت کو اجرت پر لے جو ماں کے پاس رہ کر دودھ پلائے۔
او پر آیت گزری کہ باپ پر بچے کا نفقہ لازم ہے۔ وعلى المولود له رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف (الف) (آیت ۲۳۳ سورة البقرة ٢) اور ماں پر دودھ پلانا لازم نہیں ہے اس کے لئے اس آیت میں اشارہ ہے۔ لا تضار والدة بولدها ولا مولود له بولده (ب) آیت ۲۳۳ سورة البقرة (۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ والدہ کو دودھ پلانے میں نقصان نہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ اور دوسری عورت کو دودھ پلانے کے لئے اجرت پر لے اس کے لئے یہ آیت ہے۔ وان اردتم ان تستر ضعوا اولادكم فلا جناح عليكم اذا سلمتم ما آتیتم بالمعروف (ج ) ( آیت ۲۳۳ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے پتہ چلا کہ دودھ پلانے کے لئے کسی عورت کو اجرت پر لے۔ اور چونکہ پرورش کا حق ماں کو ہے اس لئے ماں کے پاس رہ کر دودھ پلائے ۔
(۲۱۵۷) (۳۰) اگر اجرت پر لیا بیوی کو یا اپنی عدت گزارنے والی کو تا کہ اس کے بچے کو دودھ پلائے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔
ا شوہر نے اپنی بیوی یا طلاق کی عدت گزارنے والی کو اجرت پر لیا تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہ بچے کی ماں ہے اس لئے اگر مجبوری نہ ہو تو اس کو ہی دودھ پلانا چاہئے ۔ اور جب اجرت لیکر دودھ پلانے پر تیار ہوئی تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس کو دودھ پلانے کی مجبوری نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو اجرت پر لینا جائز نہیں ہے (۲) آیت میں ہے کہ والدہ کو دودھ پلانا چاہئے۔ والوالدات يرضعن اولادهن حولين كاملين لمن اراد ان يتم الرضاعة ( و ) ( آیت ۲۳۳ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ والد ہ دودھ پلائے اس لئے اپنی والدہ کو اجرت پر لینا ٹھیک نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ نفقہ وغیرہ لے رہی ہے۔
2157. (30) If he hires her while she is his wife or in her 'iddah to nurse his child, it is not permissible. (31) And if her 'iddah ends and he hires her for nursing, it is permissible. (32) And if the father says, 'I will not hire her,' and brings another woman, and the mother agrees to the same wage as the foreign woman, then the mother has more right (to nurse). And if she requests more, the husband is not forced (to pay it).
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Kitab al-Nafaqat. The primary ruling is that a father cannot hire his own wife or a woman in 'iddah to nurse his child if the child is from him, because the nurse is the child's mother and is already obliged to nurse without wage if she is not incapacitated. The Quranic verses cited show that the father is responsible for provision, the mother should not be harmed by being forced to nurse, and hiring a wet nurse is permissible. The commentary clarifies that hiring one's wife or a divorcée in 'iddah is invalid because she is already providing nursing as a duty; accepting wage implies she is not obliged.

Key Terms
استئجار (isti'jar): Hiring a person for a wage to perform a service, here specifically nursing.
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman observing 'iddah after divorce or death of husband.
رضاع (rada'): The act of breastfeeding a child by a woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not permissible to hire one's wife to nurse their child according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because the wife is not required to nurse.
B) Because she is already obliged to nurse without wage.
C) Because hiring any relative is invalid.
D) Because the child belongs to both parents.

Key Takeaway
A father cannot hire his wife or a woman in 'iddah to nurse his child because she is already obligated to nurse without wage; the contract is fasid.

beginner

Hiring After 'Iddah is Permissible
Ruling on hiring ex-wife after 'iddah for nursing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a divorcée for nursing after her 'iddah and explain the legal reasoning for the change in permissibility.

Core Idea
Once 'iddah ends, the woman is a stranger; hiring her is permissible.

In the previous passage, it was forbidden for a father to hire his divorced wife for nursing during her 'iddah because she was obligated to nurse for free. But once the 'iddah ends, the obligation ceases, and she becomes like any other woman. The author explains the reasoning: she is no longer a wife nor receiving maintenance, so hiring her is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage states: 'if her 'iddah ends and he hires her, it is permissible.' The condition is the completion of 'iddah.
2
Understand the legal reason (ta'lil)
The commentary explains: she is no longer a wife, not receiving maintenance, so she is like a stranger—thus the general permissibility of hiring applies.
3
Apply the principle
When an impediment (the obligation to nurse for free) ceases, the default permissibility of hiring returns.
4
Contrast with the previous prohibition
During 'iddah, she was obligated to nurse and entitled to maintenance, so hiring would be redundant and invalid. After 'iddah, those cease.
This demonstrates how rulings change with legal status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۱۵۸] (۳۱) اور اگر اس کی عدت ختم ہو گئی اور اس کو اجرت پر لیا دودھ پلانے کے لئے تو جائز ہے۔ بیوی عدت گزار رہی تھی اس دوران عدت ختم ہو گئی۔ اب اس کو اپنے بچے کے دودھ پلانے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا تو جائز ہے۔
اب یہ بیوی نہیں رہی اور نہ شوہر سے نفقہ لے رہی ہے بلکہ اجنبیہ بن گئی اس لئے اس کو اجرت پر لینا جائز ہے۔
2158. (31) And if her 'iddah ends and he hires her for nursing, it is permissible. The wife was observing 'iddah, during which the 'iddah ended. Now he hires her to nurse his child, it is permissible. Now she is no longer a wife, not receiving maintenance from the husband, but has become a stranger, so hiring her is permissible.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This is a continuation of the ruling. The exception to the previous prohibition: when the woman's 'iddah expires, she is no longer legally connected to the husband. The obligation to nurse without wage ceases because she is no longer entitled to maintenance from him. Thus, she becomes like any other woman, and hiring her for nursing is valid.

Key Terms
انقضاء العدة (inqida' al-'iddah): The completion of the waiting period after divorce or death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does hiring a divorcée become permissible?
A) Immediately after divorce.
B) After her 'iddah ends.
C) Only if she remarries.
D) Never.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of hiring a divorced woman for nursing depends on whether her 'iddah has ended; after 'iddah, she is a stranger and can be hired.

beginner

Mother's Priority to Nurse for Equal Wage
Ruling on mother's right to nurse when father brings a stranger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mother's priority to nurse and apply the condition that she must accept the same wage as a stranger.

Core Idea
A mother's right to nurse her child is conditional on accepting the same wage as a stranger; she cannot demand more.

This lesson addresses a common family law scenario: when a father wants to hire a wet nurse but the mother also wishes to nurse. The Hanafi school balances the mother's natural attachment and the prohibition against harming her with the father's right not to be overcharged. The key is the mother's acceptance of the market wage.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling scenario
Identify the situation: the father refuses to hire the mother and brings a stranger (foreign woman) to nurse. The mother then offers to nurse for the same wage as the stranger.
This is the default case for the mother's priority.
2
Apply the condition of equal wage
If the mother agrees to the same wage, she has the right to nurse and must be given priority. If she demands more, the father is not forced to accept.
The father is not compelled to pay above market rate.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is from Quran 2:233: 'لَا تُضَآرَّ وَالِدَةُۢ بِوَلَدِهَا وَلَا مَوۡلُودٞ لَّهُۥ بِوَلَدِهِۦ' – no harming of mother nor father through the child.
The verse prohibits harming either parent.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Giving the mother the child at the same wage avoids harming her; forcing the father to pay more would harm him. Thus the ruling balances both harms.
The same verse supports both rights.
5
Note the boundary
If the mother asks for more, the father may hire the stranger. The mother's priority is not absolute – it is tied to the market wage.
This prevents exploitation of the father.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۱۵۹) (۳۲) اور اگر باپ نے کہا نہیں اجرت پر لوں گا والدہ کو اور کسی دوسری عورت کو لے آئے ، پس ماں راضی ہوگئی اجنبیہ کی اجرت مثل پر تو ماں اس کی زیادہ حقدار ہوگی۔ اور اگر وہ اجرت زیادہ طلب کرے تو شوہر کو اس پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
بچے کی والدہ عدت گزار کر اجنبیہ ہو چکی تھی۔ اب باپ کہتا ہے کہ میں بچے کو دودھ پلانے کے لئے اس کو اجرت پر نہیں لاؤں گا۔ اب اگر والدہ اتنی ہی اجرت پر راضی ہو جاتی ہے جتنی اجنبیہ لیتی ہے تو والدہ اجرت لینے اور دودھ پلانے کی زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ والدہ کو بچے سے زیادہ محبت ہے اس لئے وہ زیادہ پیار سے پالے گی اس لئے وہ زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ اور اگر اس کو نہیں دیتے ہیں تو اس کو نقصان ہوگا اور والدہ کو نقصان دینے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ لا تضار والدة بولدها ولا مولود له بولده (الف) (آیت ۲۳۳ سورة البقر۲) اور اگر اجنبیہ عورت سے زیادہ اجرت مانگے تو باپ کو اس پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا کہ والدہ کو زیادہ اجرت دے کر لاؤ۔ کیونکہ اس سے والد کو نقصان ہوگا ۔ اور آیت میں والد کو نقصان دینے سے منع فرمایا۔ اوپر آیت میں تھا۔ ولا مولود له بولدہ اس لئے :
باپ کو زیادہ اجرت دینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
التمس : مانگنا، تلاش کرنا۔
2159. (32) And if the father says, 'I will not hire her,' and brings another woman, and the mother agrees to the same wage as the foreign woman, then the mother has more right (to nurse). And if she requests more, the husband is not forced (to pay).
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This ruling balances rights. The mother has a preferential right to nurse her own child due to maternal affection and the prohibition of harming her. However, if she demands a higher wage than the market rate, the father is not compelled to accept, as that would harm him—also prohibited by the same verse. Thus, she gets priority only at the prevailing wage.

Key Terms
الأحقية (al-ahaqqiyyah): The entitlement or priority, here the mother's right to nurse the child if she offers the same terms as a stranger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the mother demands a higher wage than a stranger?
A) Father must pay because she is the mother.
B) Father is not forced to pay more.
C) The child is taken away from both.
D) Mother loses all right to nurse.

Key Takeaway
The mother's priority to nurse is conditional on accepting the same wage as a stranger, balancing the Quranic prohibition of harming either parent.
